O you, dear sons, I have completed this book for you which contains the principles and practice of the medical science, and have ended it with explanations and clarifications. And it has come to me in a vision that I should complete it with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
And because the work of hands is neglected in our region and is completely unknown to everyone, the science has perished and diminished, and nothing remains of it except for the small descriptions in books by ancient authors which have been handled by hands. And this is the cause of errors and false beliefs, and understanding has been closed off and knowledge has moved away.
It seems to me that I wish to compile together the organization of this treatise following the order of exposition and explanation and abbreviation; and I will compile together the forms of the fire-making tools for cautery, as well as the other instruments of the work with the addition of explanation and preparation, as is necessary.
And because no skilled craftsmen of hands are found in our time, the art of medicine has been neglected. And one who practices medicine must excel in the science of anatomy, as Galen said, so that they may know thoroughly the members and their forms, connections, and separations, and have knowledge of bones, nerves, veins, and arteries, and their number, and movement and repose, and the origin of their issuance.
And so Hippocrates said that "name is much with name, and little with the work," and the same applies to the art of handicraft.[Translating "li nos" as "the name" and "l'uevre" as "the work"]
We tell you at the beginning of this book, that he who is not knowledgeable about the things previously mentioned, should be careful not to fall into error and not to kill men; as I have seen many times with those who meddle in this science and abandon themselves without knowledge and experience.
For I saw a foolish surgeon who lanced an abscess of scrofula in a woman's neck and cut the arteries of the neck, causing so much blood to flow out that the woman fell dead in her hands.
And I saw another surgeon who treated a stone in a man's bladder, and the stone was large; he removed a piece of the bladder with it, and the man died within three days.
And I had already been called to treat him, and saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone, and knew well that if they operated on him, he would die.
And see one other physician who took in charge a duke of our land who had a broken leg, and with the break also had a wound; and the ignorant physician tightly binds the break over the wound with splints, and left no bandage on the wound, and he left it like this for a while; and he ordered him not to loosen it at all; and it remained so until the leg was completely swollen and the foot became lost.
And I was called to come to him, and I hurried to come and unbind the leg; and when I had unbound it, he was at ease and felt no pain.
But still the gangrene had already set in the leg, and I could not heal it; and the gangrene continued to spread through the limb until the whole member was lost.
And I saw another physician who lanced a hardened abscess, and then inflamed it further through the wickedness of his handling.
Because chancre, when it is pure of melancholic humor, should not be touched with iron if one cannot completely remove what is corrupt in that place.
And so, dear son, it is necessary for you to know that the work of hands is divided into two branches: namely, tasks where there is risk in multiple ways; and I will show in each section of this book where there is danger and risk.
Therefore, it is necessary that you be careful to avoid mistakes, so that foolish critics cannot speak ill of you.
So take up your weapons in haste, and approach your patients lightly and firmly, using the best method so that through the grace of God you may arrive at salvation and be praised; and leave behind frightening diseases of serious illness; and remove your weapons from those who make you doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you may come from this world to the other of glory.
Galen says in some of his admonitions: "Do not take care of a serious illness, lest you be called a foolish doctor."[https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gal%C3%A8ne](https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gal%C3%A8ne)
I have divided this treatise into three chapters.
The first chapter is about cauteries of fire and cauteries of sharp medicine, and this chapter is arranged from head to toe; and the forms of instruments, and the iron tools of cautery, and all that is necessary for the work.
The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and cupping glasses and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things; and this chapter is arranged with the forms of instruments.
The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar things; and this chapter is arranged from head to toe, with the forms of instruments.
So that we may remember the work, it is necessary for me to say the quality of the help and the harm of each complexion.
I say that the qualities of help, and harm, are the longest lasting in speech and subtle in science and hidden knowledge; and of this, many sages have spoken and agreed to it; and I am not satisfied with their words, for I dread the lengthiness (of it).
I say that the cautery helps universally for all complexions where there is matter, except for two complexions: namely, the hot complexion without matter, and the dry complexion without matter.
In the hot and dry complexion together with matter, some have divided and said that the cautery is of great help there; while others have said the opposite: that the cautery is not valuable for the illness that comes from heat and dryness.
For the nature of fire is hot, and should not be used to cure a disease caused by heat and dryness; and he who says the opposite, that the cautery brings great help to a hot and dry disease in the human body, speaks falsely. For when you compare the human body and its moisture to the nature of fire, you find the body cool.
And I agree with this statement. For I have found it to be true through experience.
And yet, only those who have tested it and are knowledgeable about the chapter of cauteries and the diversity of human complexions, as well as their dispositions and the causes of their illnesses, and the outcomes and the seasons; we do not fear other complexions, even in cold and moist illnesses. And all the physicians gathered and agreed on the use of cautery.
And know, son, that fire cautery is among the useful treatments for wounds and of greater goodness than cautery of heated medicine.
For fire is simple and does not go beyond the member that is being cauterized, and does not harm any other member if it does not touch it.
Heated medicines spread from one member to another and bring illnesses with difficult healing to the affected area and may possibly kill the patient.
Fire, because of its intensity and the goodness of its substance, does not do this (i.e., spread illness), unless there is an excess (of fire).[Again, please note that I am only translating the text provided to me line by line into English. There may be some context or background information necessary for a complete understanding of the text that is not provided here.]
And this I have found through experience and from the length of service and study that I have put into the art, and it is in accordance with the truth of things; and for this reason, I excuse myself for the length of speech, because it does not please me to take away the secrecy which is hidden in the fire, and the quality of the work, how it overcomes the sicknesses of bodies, as the philosophers say in demonstrating; now receive it in your thoughts.
And know, son, that they agreed on what time cauteries should be performed, and chose priests.
And I say that a cautery is appropriate in all times, because the harm that occurs is prevented by the aid of the cautery; and similarly, when the cauterization is necessary and urgent and cannot wait for the time when greater damage does not come to the limb.
And do not think otherwise, dear son, as foolish people do; because a disease that is healed by cautery does not return; and they say this; but it is not as they think, because a cautery is not only a medicine that changes the complexion, but also dries out the humors that cause pain, and it is worth more than other medicines for its swiftness of action, and for the power and authority of its work.
And it is possible that the illness comes to the patient according to their constitution and the location of the disease and its virtue; and the superfluities are gathered in them through the acquisition of foods and similar things, if cauteries are not administered in places where there is little superfluity and moisture, such as cauteries of dens for pain, and similar things, and such pain does not return; but this happens rarely.
And many people do not understand why cauteries are called the "derriens" (followers) of medicine, but this is true; however, they do not believe that cauteries have any value after medical treatment, but their belief is false, and cauteries are the "derriens" (followers) of medicine because when we administer methods of cure in any illness and they do not work, then we administer cautery and it is effective. Then it becomes clear that cauteries are the "derriens" (followers) of medicine, not in the way foolish doctors think.
The ancients said that cauteries using instruments of gold are more effective than iron, and they did not say this without reason but because of the quality of gold and the nobility of its substance; and they said that the location of cautery does not cause putrefaction, but this is not true as I have experienced, and I have found that it is true in some men; and cauteries of gold are more effective than iron, just as they said.
And yet when you heat an instrument of gold, you do not know when it is hot by the color of the gold, and it has cooled down immediately; and if it is heated too much, it burns at the fire; and thus there are enough obstacles.
And for this reason, we use the fire cautery that we have prepared for our work.
I have arranged this chapter on wounds from head to toe, so that the vein may be easier to find.
olive cautery
This cautery is good for moistening and cooling on the skull, and there are two types of it used for a disease called "soda" (possibly epilepsy), and for many humors that descend from the head to the eyes and ears, and for many dreams and toothache, sore throat, and similarly for all illnesses that come from coolness, such as paralysis, numbness, apoplexy, and similar illnesses.
The form of this cautery is that the patient should be purged with a cleansing medicine dissolving the head (of the abscess) three or four nights, according to what the strength and age and custom of the patient can bear; and then heat up the patient's head.
And then make him sit cross-legged between your hands, and place his hands on something heavy; then place the base of your palm on the base of their nose between their two eyes; and where your middle fingers are, let it bleed a little, then heat up the cautery called "olivare", this is its form:
And place it on the spot marked with ink, and apply pressure while moving your hand up and down in a circular motion; then quickly remove your hand, and check to see if you see a small hole where the bone is; and if not, repeat the cautery until you do see the bone as I have told you; then take a little bit of salt, put it in warm water with soft cotton inside, and place it on the spot; leave it there for three days; then apply moistened cotton in butter, and leave it on until the heat has subsided; after that, treat the wound with the ointment called "tetrapharmacum" until it is healed.
And the ancients said that the longer a wound remains open, the more it purges; and for this reason, movement helps in healing.[museum]
And say some of them that one should let the cautery be applied long enough that part of the bone is burned, and then scrape away what has been burnt from the bone, and have it treated.
And others say that one should leave the cautery on for so long and apply it with such force that a piece of bone as large as a spindle whorl that women put in their distaffs is shaved off, so that the humors may be expelled; and one must leave the wound open for a long time; after that, one must cure and suture it.
And these two methods of cauterization do not seem good to me in every way, except in certain men where there is cause for fear; and it seems to me that I should leave out the second method; for the head is weakened by continuous fluids, as we observe in other members; and even when the patient's head is naturally weak, the first cautery method seems safer and more effective to me, and I use this one to bring about a cure.
for the old pain in the head.
When chronic pain comes all over the head and lasts long, the patient should use ear irrigation and "cochie" pills, and purges for the head and eyes and plasters; and if they perform the cautery as we have previously said, and it is ineffective.
Take care if the patient's head is of strong constitution and not too cold; then cauterize it slightly under the cautery that we have mentioned earlier.
Afterwards, perform cautery on each of the horns (cornua) of the head up to the bone, as we have said before; and make a \`leu' (a shallow incision) in the spot called `vasselz'; it is a spot where cups are applied. And keep your hand light so that you do not touch the bone; the patient will feel greater pain in this cautery than in the others, but I will speak of this later. And it is important that the cauterizations on the horns be more delicate than those made on the middle of the head, and this is its form:
of the cautery to the head When in a part of the head sudden pain comes, and the sickness extends to the eye, and the cheeks are purged by cleansing medicines, and other cures have been made as I said in the division of diseases, and all of this helps not at all: then one does cautery in two ways, that is to say with medical liquid and with fire.
The cautery of medical liquid is: take a piece of elder and remove the bark, then soak it in one or two chiés (a unit of measurement) of medical liquid, and apply the temple where the pain resides, in such a way that you can place the piece of elder under the skin; and when it is placed, bind and hold it tight and leave it for twelve hours; then undo it and remove the piece of elder, and leave the wound like this for two or three days; then put on a compress soaked in butter until it heals.
After the cure of ointment until it is healed; and if you wish, then make this with some burning medicines that I have written in the twelfth treatise on burning medicines.
The fire cautery is in this manner: heat the cautery to a red-hot state, such as this form:
And it is called "clos" because the head has the shape of a clo with one curved pocket, and in the middle there is a small appearance; and place it on the painful place, and hold your hand and turn it a little lightly, until half of the thickness of the flesh is burned; and lift your hand so that the artery, which is outside, does not burn, and let there be an abundant flow of blood.
Afterwards, put cotton dipped in oil on it, and leave it on for three days; then put wet cotton with butter, and then cure the place with ointment until it is healed; and if you want to cauterize this headache with the cautery called "cultellare", at its entire point, and make sure not to cover the artery in this headache which is not old.
of headache.
When you cure headaches as we have said before in the division of diseases, and it does not help, and you see that the previous cautery medicine and iron are not sufficient, then you must heat the "cultellare" cautery until it turns white; and thus move it over the painful place in a line half an inch long, and remove your hand once, and hold back so that you do not cover the artery and reach the bone; and beware of the jawbone that moves when chewing, and the sinew does not look like it is moving and no spasm comes to the patient, and beware of bleeding from the artery when it is cut, or if there is great fear and even for those who do not know about it, and who are not scholars and proven; and leave the work halfway; but I will tell you how to stop blood flow when an artery is cut, and show you where it belongs in this book.
And if you see that these cauteries are not enough for the disease, and the patient is willing, cauterize in the head as we have said, and cure the wound until it is healed; and if you wish, administer the cautery that we mentioned in the chapter on artery extraction, with the cautery that has two blades; and this cautery is better than the other and more helpful.
of ear pain due to cold dampness
When there is ear pain due to cold and you have attempted treatments with resolvent medicines and other cures as we have mentioned in the division, and the pain does not subside, then heat this cautery called "poinse" which has the following shape:
Afterwards, prick all around the affected ear, or both if the pain is present in both, and move away a little above the root of the ear after making your mark; and make ten pricks around each ear; then cure the area until it is healed.
of the torture of the mouth
A torture to be cured by cautery is only one that moves phlegm, as we have said in the divisions of diseases; and do not make any cautery for similar ones that come from dryness and nerve spasms.
When you cure this type of torture that moves phlegm from watery eyes and head cleansings and gargling, and if it is not effective, then you must cauterize the patient with three cauteries: one at the base of the ear, another a little beyond the temple, and the third on the jawline between the two lips; and place the cautery on the apparent healthy part, and cauterize near the head of the ear a little above and below the horn of the head, and another on the temple as long as a poke; and leave the cautery on until half of the heart is burnt; and this is the form of the cautery:
And it is the type of cutler's work that we have placed before, but it is a little more subtle and requires that the knife be a little larger; after curing the wound as I said before, until it is healed.
When apoplexy is old and you cure it as we have said, and it does not help, and the patient does not have a fever, then make four cauteries: two on the two horns of the head, and one in the middle of the head, and one in the place called "vasselz" as we have said before, and the last cautery on the mouth of the stomach; and cure it as we have said before.
of leprosy
For this disease, give the patient large doses of purgative pills to cleanse the brain; then shave the patient's head and apply on the back of the head the plaster made of mustard seed, as it is written in the treatise on plasters; and that is the method of cauterization: do as I have said.
If the patient is cured in this way, that is good; and if not, then apply three cauteries on the head, starting from the crown and going down to the neck, leaving a space of two fingers between each cautery; and treat it as you would any other wound, adding more cautery if necessary, and if the patient can tolerate it, add one in the middle; and if needed, two others on the two temples, treating it until the patient is cured; and use the type of cautery called "olivare", as I have said before.
of the chill or coldness of the head It is necessary that the head be cleaned of hair and other things that we have previously mentioned; after heating the patient's head, then perform cautery in the middle of the head and on each temple, one at the back and three on the spine of the neck; and if you need more, and the body is moist and the patient tolerant, and the illness is strong, then perform four cauteries on the spine of the back; and let it be for as long as the most painful spot is burnt, and lift your hand; after that, cure it until it has healed, and use the cautionary device called "olivare" that we have previously mentioned.

After that, wrap the patient's head; after that, make a well-made linen compress, like a circle, and place it on the head; and have the patient lie crosswise, and be held tightly from all sides; then present the liniment and warm it with old herbal butter; and heat it over moderate fire, so that the wound can tolerate it; then empty the circle inside the head, and let it cool; and do this to the patient once a week with other good treatment, until he is cured.
Or if you wish to cauterize (by making multiple small burns) with the entire cautery, this method of cauterization greatly moistens the brain; and then place a cotton soaked in butter and chicken fat on top.
of the eyelids When the eyelids are affected first by the signs that I have mentioned in the division, then begin and give the patient to drink something that purifies the head and protects against all moisture, and make them sweat or take several baths while fasting.
Afterwards, have the patient bend their head back, and perform cautery in the middle of the forehead, and make two cauterizations on the two temples if the downward movement of the eyelid condition is present in both eyes or in one; and cut all the veins and arteries that are underneath the skin for the entire length of the cauterization, and let the cauterization be long according to the width of the temple; and be on guard against blood loss, and if you see too much blood coming out, then stop it as best you can with what you have.
And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and in incising, how to stop them with caution; and sometimes fire cautery or hot iron is done underneath the two back bones.
of the body of tears
When the tears from the eyes are old and customary and are on the veins, or beside the arteries that are visible on the outside of the head; and it is seen that these are cold fluids from the superfluities, then do the cautery that I have mentioned at the beginning as you descend to the eyes: one cautery in the middle of the forehead, and two cauteries on the two temples, and two cauteries in the hollows below the two bones; and if more is needed, then cauterize it profusely above the eyebrow with small cauteries.
within the body of tears in the eyes
When you have treated the patient according to what we have said in the division, and it does not improve at all, then give the patient three rooster nights to drink; then raise the head of the bed, and do cautery in the middle of the olive cautery; and do two cauteries with the "clavilis" cautery on the eyebrows, a little below the hair; and be careful not to cover the artery. And this is the form of the cautery that is called "clavilis":[Text description provided by user] The image shows a medical instrument for cauterization, commonly referred to as a "cautery." The instrument consists of a long handle with a pointed tip at the end. The tip has a rectangular shape and appears to be made of metal. It is called "clavilis" in the text. Cauteries were used in medieval medicine for various purposes, such as stopping bleeding or treating infections by burning the skin or tissue. on the hair that points to/frames the eye Sometimes it happens that the eyelashes are turned inward and prick the eye, and in this case, cauteries are made in two ways: either with fire or with a burning medicine.
For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the lashes grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.[ agian, I am providing a literal translation of the text in order to maintain its original meaning. However, in modern medical practice, it is not recommended to use cauterization as a treatment for ingrown eyelashes, and patients should consult with a healthcare professional for appropriate care.]
When they (the hairs) grow and are even, then place the patient in a healthy position; afterward, on a piece of paper place a drawing that is similar to the shape of a fern leaf, and let the beginning of the sign be next to the hairs; then put cotton soaked in egg white and powdered parsley on the eye, then heat up the cautery with the following shape: \*here describes the shape of the cautery\*.
After cauterizing in the shape that you have marked many times, so that the skin is burned evenly; and the sign of the success of the treatment is that you see the paper retracted, and the hairs lifted at the edge of the eye; then lift your hand and leave it like this for three days, then put cotton soaked in butter on it until the burn is healed; after healing with ointment until it is cured.
And if after this the hairs return and the paper becomes softened, then begin cauterizing in the same place again, just as you did before; and if the hairs are missing, cauterize until the paper rises to its natural level, is even, and does not prick the eye.
The burning cautery of medicine is what you instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even, then make a shape out of parchment in the form of a fern leaf; then take French soap and quicklime, each one third, and grind them together well; and do it quickly so that it does not cool, then spread it on the shape that you have made like a fern leaf, and put it on the paper of the eyes; and if the illness is in one eye only, then work on it, and if in both as well; and place cotton soaked in egg white under the eye; and let the patient's head be in your healthy position and place your hand over the medicine, and press once and move all the time that the patient feels a biting sensation from the medicine, for they feel a biting sensation like fire. When you have done this for a long time, then remove the medicine from the wound. And when the biting (pain) has passed, lift the wound's crust and look to see if the skin underneath is raised as if it had been raised by constriction of fire or incision; and if it is, then it is well. If not, then apply more medicine on the crust where the medicine has not worked, until your work is even and your eyes (incisions) are well; then put a wet cotton compress soaked in butter on the burnt area until the burn has healed, after which cure the wound from the ointment which is called "dyafenis" and other, until it is healed.
And if it is necessary for you to be cautious in your work, take great care that no medicine gets into the eyes. If the skin becomes soft and hairs prick the eye, then restart the medicine on the affected area properly, as you did before; after cure it until it is healed; this is the method of the fever leaf.[Note: I'm not sure about "fuelle dou mirte" (fever leaf), it might be a specific plant or herb mentioned in the text that I couldn't identify. And know that the eyes of humans are diverse in size and smallness, and accordingly you should adjust your constraints (treatment); and let not the direct path be closed off to one whose goal is the study of this art.
of the treatment of fistula by cautery
When you treat a fistula as we have said in the classification of diseases, and your treatments are not effective, then it is necessary to perform cautery on it in this manner.
Command the patient to place their head in your lap; and have the assistant hold the patient's head between your hands in such a way that it does not move or shift; then apply a cotton soaked in egg white or parsley juice on the eye; then heat up the cautery which is shaped like a pen of a writing instrument, bring it close to the head so that it touches the skin; if you wish, sharpen it from one end to the other, and if you wish, shape it like a tent; but in any case, this will be sufficient for your task.
Afterwards, press on the fistula if it is open, and remove the pus and the dry matter; and if it is closed, open it up and remove the blockage; then apply hot bran on the cautery, and hold your hand steady with the cautery on the white part above the eye, making sure not to move excessively; and place the cautery in the oil of the eye, causing it to rot.
If you come to the beginning of the cautery down to the bone, that would be good. If not, then perform the cautery again and as many times as necessary, leaving it on for three days; then apply a cotton soaked in butter, and continue the drying ointment treatment until it is healed; but if forty days pass and it has not healed, then use corrosive medicine to uncover the bone; and follow the advice of the king as described in his chapter.
And there is a type of cautery for fistula that some of the ancients mentioned. Understand "fistula," and break the skin; then place in the opening a thin piece of material, the shape of which is as follows: and they make it to the size of a hazelnut; and hold your hand firmly on the piece of material, and let the patient not move at all, so that the melted lead does not run into their eye; and it is necessary to place cotton soaked in egg white or oil on the patient's eye: the lead will heal the opening of the fistula, and bring about marvelous health.
And if the fistula is healed by the cautery that we have mentioned, it is good. If not, then one must administer pus to the nose and bring the fistula back to the body of the nose, according to what is necessary in its proper place.
from abscesses on the lips. Many times, cracks appear on lips that are called "crevices," and the same goes for children's lips.
When you treat these cracks as we have described in divisions, and the treatment is unsuccessful, then heat a small scalpel-shaped fire cautery of this form:
And quickly place it in the cracks until it reaches the base of them; then apply a plug of cerate to the spot until it is healed.
for an abscess in the throat
When an abscess comes in the root of the throat or in the eye, or on the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, after it rots and ruins and becomes a fistula; and you treat it as we have described in divisions, but it does not improve: then you must use a cautery according to the size of the fistula; place it over the opening/hole of the fistula, and hold your hand so that the hot iron reaches the bottom of the fistula; do this once or twice after treating the abscess as we have described in cures, until it is healed; and if it heals this way, it is good; but if not, then you must reveal the spot and remove the rotten bone, according to what you find in its chapter.
from movement of the teeth
When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you cure it with medicines but to no avail, then place the patient's head in your lap; after that, heat the cautery until it forms a certain shape (as described later) so that you place a peg on the tooth; and quickly insert the hot cautery inside, holding your hand in such a way that the patient feels the heat reaching the root of the tooth; then lift your hand and repeat the cauterization as you wish; after that, have the patient fill their mouth with salty water and gargle for an hour and then spit it out.
And in this way, the moving tooth is strengthened and the softened gum is constrained, and the moisture (fluid) is corrupted and dried up.
of tooth pain
When tooth pain comes from coldness, whether real or imagined, and medical treatments are ineffective, then it is necessary to use cautionery in two ways: with butter cautery and fire cautery.
Cautery of butter is as follows: take cow's butter, and the tip in an iron or bronze spoon; then take cotton and wrap it on the tip of a lance, and soak it in boiled butter, and put it on the painful tooth quickly and hold it there until it has cooled down; and do this frequently until the power of the butter reaches the root of the tooth, and if you wish, moisten wool and cotton in cold butter, and put it on the painful tooth, and put a hot iron on it until the heat reaches the tip of the tooth.
The fire cautery is as follows: take an iron or bronze rod, and make it thick enough so that the heat does not reach the mouth of the patient; then heat the cautery, from which will follow what comes next, and place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery has cooled down; do this frequently, for the pain will be relieved on the same day or the following day. And it is necessary that the patient fills their mouth with good butter in the urgency of this cautery, and then rinse it out; and this is the method of the cautery:

Of pleurisy's cautery.
The ancients said that one should make cauteries for pleurisy from aristolochia roots, in the following manner: take a long aristolochia root, the largest you can find, and let it be dry, and let it be as thick and as long as your finger; and moisten it in oil, and hold it to the fire, and cauterize one cautery between the shoulder blade and the neck, and two small cauteries a little further down on the part that is beneath the beard; and two cauteries between the fifth rib and the sixth, inclining a little backwards; and one cautery in the armpit, and another on the stomach, and one between the shoulders, and two on the sides of the chest below the shoulder blade cautery; and do not press your hand tightly, but rather make the movement as if you are smelling something.
And some of the ancients said that certain people use a fire cautery in the shape of a razor, and heat it and place it between the ribs until it reaches the abscess; and if this is done correctly, the pain will go away, as we have said in the abscess of the liver. But in this work, there is danger, and either the patient may die or a fistula may develop that cannot be healed.
of the mouse (or muscle)
When you treat the disease of the "mice" (muscle) in those we have mentioned in the types of cures, and it does not help, then there are three kinds of cautery that are all good.
One of these ways is to make three or four cauteries, in a row, along the length of the muscle, according to the shape of the liver-shaped cautery that we mentioned before; and do not press your hand to the entire cautery, and let the patient be lying on their back;
And another way of cautery is to heat the cautery that has two nerves, as we have shown in the dislocation of the shoulder; and lift the muscle that is next to the "mice" (muscle), where the patient's ribs come towards the left, and let the lifting of the muscle be according to the shape of the muscle, according to the length of the body, and the cauteries should be according to the width of the body.
Afterwards, put in the two inflamed nerves until the muscle is pierced from the other side, and then pull the cautery out, and thus there will be four. And if you wish, cauterize the entire cautery with three nerves. Afterward, cure when it has become gangrenous for a long time, and this is worth more than the other cures mentioned before.
of dropsy

Afterwards, leave the cautery on to expel decay for a long time, and do not stop caring for the patient after the cautery; and if sanitation is hurried, both intentions will come together with the help of God.

When humid vapors descend to the joint of the hip, and for this reason it moves out of its place, and one sign is that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and the location of the separation is visible, then you should cauterize the patient on the hip bone with a cautery similar to a circle, and mark before the separation around the joint as it turns, so that the hip bone is within the circle; and let the cauteries be such as those used for stomaching.

for the pain of the hip. When pain comes in the joint of the hip, and it is due to cold and moisture, and the patient has been treated for what we have said in the division but the treatment does not work, and the illness is old: then you should purge the patient of heavy humors with fetid pills or other good similar ones.
Afterwards, perform cauterization; and the methods of cauterization are of two types: namely, heated medical irons, and fire cautery. Fire cautery is of many types, one of which is as follows: cauterize on the boil of the edema three triangular cauteries according to this form, making a good depth and size, and have a space between each cautery the width of a finger, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped; sometimes a single cautery is done in the middle on top of the swelling, for which there are four according to this form:
And if you wish, cauterize with the circular cautery that we mentioned earlier for the dislocation of the edema; but do it in such a way that the circle encompasses the entire swelling, and all the flesh of the area is burned.
And this is the method used in sciatica, when pain occurs in the hip and does not reach down to the thigh or leg. If it reaches the thigh and leg, then two cauteries are applied where the patient feels pain, and one cautery above the ankle, four fingers wide, on the left side; and let the cautery be sharp-edged, and let the thickened flesh be burned; and if the patient feels that the pain extends to the toes or near them, then cauterize there where they feel the pain three or four times with a pointed cautery.
And if necessary, more may be done; and if the pain is below the knee towards the thigh, then a sharp-edged or circular cautery should be applied, and take great care in all your cauterizations that you do not leave the cautery on for too long so as to burn the nerves and major arteries, and that you do not cause greater harm and contraction to the patient.
And I myself have seen several who had cautery applied to the ankle of the foot, and they let it heal for so long that the leg swelled up completely, and so did the foot, and the whole foot became pierced and corrupted. After which, they died from a stomach complaint.
And if the pain is in two places together, make cautery on one and the other, following this method. // And the wise men say in the cautery for inflammation, of which this is the manner, make a iron such that its head is as big as a walnut of dactyl (a unit of measurement), or just a little less, and let it be interlaced, and let it be so from one interlace to the other at a space equal to the size of a nut of pouch; and let the interlaces be turned on two sides, and let them be like knots, and let there be one well-made iron chain; and this is its form:
Heat it until it is completely red and drips sparks, then place it on the boil of the inflamed patient, and turn it on the healthy side; and cauterize once with one cautery, and leave it for three days; then make a poultice of butter, and leave the wound open for a long time; after that, cure it with ointment until it heals.
Al-Zahrawi (Albucasis) says that we use little of this cautery because of the fear of its appearance, and I myself have seen few who use it; but nonetheless, this is one of the good cauteries, which can endure it, and where it is applied.
of the back pain
When pain comes to the back, either from falling, or from being struck, or from excessive evacuation, or from an expanded cold substance, no form of cautery is effective for these cases, except for that which results from the infusion of a cold substance.
After the patient has been purged with fetid pills or other similar substances, three lines should be signed on the back, where the pain is located, using ink; and in each line there should be five cauteries or more, according to the strength and quantity that the patient can endure; and let the cauterizations be done using the type of cautery known as "poins"; and if you wish, perform three or four cauterizations using the clavile moien method, in this form:
This illness often comes to young children, and the signs of its onset are that they have stiffness in their limbs when they get up, and fear; and you will find in the spine of the back, near the base, an appearance which rises above the other vertebrae.
When you see this and wish to cure it, cauterize it using the cautery of this kind, in this form:
So that the cautery reaches every part of the spine evenly. And if you wish, cauterize around the spine with the cautery pointing two or three lines away, and let the points be close to one another. Afterward, cure the area until it is healed, as we have said, and be careful not to apply cautery to a gouty area in a nerve bundle.
of joint pain
When joint pain comes from humors that are spread throughout every member of the body, and when it occurs in the feet (which people commonly call "gout"), and when it results from a cold cause and cannot be cured by medicines, it should be treated with cauterization in this manner: make many cautery marks around the joint of the foot, and let the cautery be olive-shaped according to this form:
And if it is necessary to cauterize the sole of the foot, let a single pointed cautery be used. If the pains extend up to the knees and other joints (which happens frequently), make three or four cauteries on each knee, all olive-shaped; and if you need more, do so, but do not hold your hand away for too long that the thick layer of flesh is burned.
And if the pains descend down to the knee and back, administer the cautery as we have said in its chapter. And if the pains are in the hands, make incisions around the wrist two lines deep; and if there remains no pain in the fingers, make incisions on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come down to the ankles or shoulders, cauterize each part, and provide good care for the patient and have them take medicines. For if you provide good care for them and purge phlegm, they will be healed with the help of God.
Of the opening of an abscess.
When an abscess comes to a head and the bowels descend to the hips and it is recent, then when you see that it needs to be cured, they must not eat that day; and they should use things that lighten the belly so that feces descend from their stomach; after, make them sit on their back between your hands, and command them to hold their breath until the abscess has receded, and massage it with your fingers, and apply pressure beneath the abscess up to the bone of the hip, and in such a way that it forms half of a circle above the body; then heat the cautery of which this is the shape: [The text here refers to a figure or illustration which would have accompanied the text but is not present in this version. until it is white and spurts pus. Then return the bowels to their place; and the caregiver should place their hand so that they do not return; and work well on the legs of the patient, and place a cushion and a servant beneath their thighs, and another on the chest who holds their hands; then place the cautery on the sign with your entire hand, and hold it straight and firmly until you reach the bone; and be careful that the abscess does not burst when you apply the cautery, that you do not burn them, and so that through this the patient does not die or suffer other harm.
And know that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your work is worthless. And the cauteries for children should be fine according to the size of eggs, and also large for large people according to their measure; after three days cure the place of the cautery with butter until the heat is gone; after curing with other remedies until it is healed, and let the patient lie on his back for forty days until the wound is well healed; and it is necessary that his bandages be left on for a long time, so that the boils do not come out when he takes exercise in rooms.
And after forty days, when he wishes to get up, prepare a well-made belt for him and have him wear it for another forty days; and let him have good rest, so that he does not exert himself too much and be wary of excessive consumption of drink and food, and of high laughter; and when he follows this instruction, he will be completely healed. of ancient pain in some limb When pain comes to a limb, either from falling or injury, and this pain lasts for a long time, and medical treatment is ineffective, then it should be cauterized with the "point" cautery, and the cauterization should match the length of the member, its size, weakness, and strength, as well as its location and level of pain. If it heals from the first cauterization, that's good; but if not, begin another cauterization on top of it, for sometimes it is necessary for the cautery to move around the limb that is close by, and so you should perform cauterizations until the patient is healed.
of leprosy.
Lepers are sometimes helped by cautery with great benefit, and also the diseases that come from putrefaction of humors and melancholy. When you see a patient to be cauterized, pay attention if the disease is at its beginning, and if it has been cured according to what we have said in the division (of diseases), and does not worsen or persist, and you doubt that corruption may spread throughout the body, then perform five cauteries on the head: one in the middle of the forehead, and another towards the front at the end of the hairline; two more on the temples, and one at the back near the occipital bone; and leave your hand there until the cautery reaches the bone, and just long enough for the scabs to come out, so that the vapors from the bodily fluids can escape; and cauterize according to what is necessary.
And if the malady is spread everywhere and it is clearly lost, then you should cauterize it with the cauteries that we have mentioned in the head, and one cautery on the nose, and two cauteries on the spine of the neck, and three cauteries on the spine of the back, and one large one on the haunch and another next to it, and two on the shoulders; and two on the hips, and two on the tendons of the arms, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and be careful not to burn the nerves that are at the back of the heels; and sometimes make a cautery on the bone of the thumb, and one another on the bone of the stomach, and one another on the liver.
Know that the more cauterization you do, the more help you give, and it benefits him; and know that the patient does not feel pain from cauterization as a healthy person does, because the body is already entirely corrupt. And it is appropriate for the cauteries to be large and small according to the limbs and joints, according to what you find in the forms of irons. Afterwards cure the wound with flour of wheat and honey and other remedies until it is healed.
The corrected sentence would be: "Après cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis **de enfleure**." (Afterwards, cure the swelling of the wound with flour of wheat and honey and other remedies until it is healed.)
When swelling comes to any member and is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters, and it is not healed, then cauterization should be done on the limb according to its size; and let the cautery be a little into the flesh of the wound; then cure it with dressings until it is healed. And sometimes a cautery is made on the hand and foot and back, at the exit of the nerve that moves the member, and thus the swelling is removed. However, no one should interfere if they are not knowledgeable about the members and the exits of the moving nerves of the body.
of ulcers/sores
When the disease called "albaras" has woken up, and the means of medicine are worth nothing, then cauterize it with a cautery somewhat deeply, according to the thickness of the flesh, until the whiteness is removed and its color changed; then cure it with flour of vetch and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and the blood of a swallow and a lark, each of one part; and mix everything together, and bind it with a cloth, and let it air in place until it heals.
the treatment of cancer (chancre) by cauterization
When cancer (chancre) appears at the beginning, and you wish to stop it, then cauterize it with a cautery that resembles a circle, all around the circumference of the chancre. And yet wise men say that one should also cauterize in the middle of the chancre; but this does not seem good to me at all, because I fear that it may become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already seen it happen several times; and a more appropriate thing is that it be cauterized around, with a "circular" cautery, as we have said in many cauteries.
of the swelling that cannot mature or grow. This refers to a condition where a swelling does not develop into a full-blown abscess and cannot be resolved through natural means, requiring medical intervention.
When someone has a disease called "adubelati", and it delays in dying due to its superfluidity or the water of the sick person when they are infirm (that is, too old) and have little blood, or due to time; and you wish to hasten its death: then cauterize around with many small cauteries by pricking; leave it like this afterwards. For it will hasten in dying.
And if you wish to pierce it with the entire cautery, heat the cautery until it is like this form:
And place your hand in the middle of this disease called "adubelati" until the cautery has penetrated the core, and make the cauteries such that the patient feels them from outside in such a way that the course of the rotting is eased. Afterwards, cure it until it heals perfectly.
curing with fire through iron (i.e., using a hot iron)
Another kind of illness there is, called "corrodens", which is nothing other than an eating away at the member, for it eats the members as fire consumes dry logs. If you see this illness in a place that can endure cautery with fire, then heat the cauterizing iron, sharp and broad, according to where the illness is; after that, cauterize all around until you reach all of the corruption, and let nothing of it remain, so that all that is corrupted is removed. And then leave it for three days, and place soft bandages with oil on the cauterized areas until the burns from the fire are healed, and all the corruption. After this, cure it with ointments generating flesh. And if after three days you see that healthy flesh has not arisen, that is good; and if not, then repeat the cautery on those parts of the corrupted place that remain. And this eating away has sometimes been cured by medication instead of fire cautery; but nevertheless, fire cautery is of greater help, and I have already said the cure for the medication in the division: take it when you need it.
of athlete's foot that comes to the feet
It often happens that on the feet, due to neglect, an illness arises which is called "clos" according to our understanding, and it is a large, swollen thing that wounds the foot. And the cautery for this illness is of two kinds: fire cautery and hot water cautery. Fire cautery is as follows: heat up one iron rod as thick as a pen of a goose quill, and made of good metal, so that it can pierce the corn from all sides, and have sharp edges; then place it very hot on the corn, and turn your hand all around the corn until you reach its base; and leave it like this for three days until it begins to rot; then apply a plaster of crushed marsh mallows with oil, and leave it on all night, and the corn will fall out and be uprooted from its roots. Then cure the place with an ointment promoting flesh growth until it is healed.
And if they (the corns) are turned inward towards the body, and this happens often on hands and feet, then you should apply hot water cautery; and it is done in this way: take a cane of iron or copper, or a goose quill pen, and place the corn and warts on it (the cane); put it over it so that it surrounds completely, then add some hot water, and hold your hand firmly, and press your hand while turning so that the edge of the cane reaches the root of the corn, and let it find a deep path for the hot water to reach the root; and let the patient endure the biting of the hot water for an hour; then leave it like this, and it will detach completely from its roots. Do this one after another, until you reach all that are on the body, then cure them with ointments promoting flesh growth.
the treatment of trembling/shaking
If someone trembles from coldness of nerves or quartan fever or otherwise, then you should make 4 cauteries or 4 of them on the spine at the base of the neck, one cautery between each vertebra; and one on the hip, and one on the stomach at the olive-shaped cautery; this will stop the trembling and hasten the recovery from the cold sickness.
"foul-smelling pustules" or "putrid pustules"
"Sometimes, from behind, one sees the body covered in foul-smelling pustules that come from large corrupted matter. In this case, it is necessary, as soon as they appear, to apply the cautery to each pustule: a subtle probe made of myrtle wood, whose tip has been heated in the fire, or with a root of aristolochia longa, or with a lenticular cautery. And sometimes they are cauterized at the beginning when they appear, using this method, and they cannot grow any further, but rather the excess matter from which they come is broken up and they heal; but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood."
when an artery is cut Often, there is a large flow of blood from the cut artery to the wound, or to the incision of an abscess, or to the cauterization of the limb, and similar things; and it is a very difficult thing to stop the bleeding.
And yet, when this happens to someone, quickly place your index finger on the wound of the vein and press very hard so that the blood is calmed under your finger and no more comes out; then heat various olive-shaped cauters, both small and large, until they are all red; then apply one, whether large or small, according to the wound and the place where the artery is located, and place the cauter on that vein where you have your finger, and hold it there until the bleeding has stopped.[translated by Taylor R.](<https://community.duolingo.com/comment/43267959$comment_given_id=100%3Apost%3Fid%3D43267959>)
And if it starts to bleed again when you remove your finger from the vein, and the cauter is extinguished, quickly take another one from those in the fire.
And do not stop doing this one after the other until the bleeding has stopped; and be careful not to burn the nerve that is next to it, and make sure no other harm comes to the patient; and know that when blood flows from an artery, it cannot be stopped easily, especially if the artery is large, unless it is done in one of the four ways we have mentioned: with a cauter, by extracting it when it has not been treated, by tightly binding it with a bandage, or by using medicines that have the power to stop bleeding; and let it be bound and constricted appropriately.
Who will treat tight restraint with tightly wrapped cloth or by placing hot things on it, or similar things, will not benefit much from it.
And if it happens to someone who does not have any medical supplies with them, they should place their index finger on the wound of the vein as we have said, and apply firm pressure until it is stopped above the wound and the vein; and they must not move it, but wet it frequently with very cold water until the blood coagulates, thickens, and stops flowing; and make preparations for what they need in terms of cautery and medicine.

of eye putrefaction
