of the veins of the eyes
There are red veins that are located over the eye and hinder the vision's function and weaken the eye all days. Therefore, it is necessary first to check if the eye, in which the veins are present, is healthy and has no other illness but sebel; then treat the eye in this manner: instruct the patient to place their head on your lap, then gently suspend those veins with your fingers according to your skill, and make sure that the fingers are gently pressed in this way:
And let there be two fingers arranged gradually in one row in this form:
then when you have carefully constricted those veins, and wiped away the blood hour after hour, until you see the swollen veins recede from the eye; and take care not to poke the eye with the ends of the cauterizing tools, and perform this task at midday before the sun, and be very diligent in your work so that you do not injure the veins; and once you have done this, distill into the eye a mixture of green and red bile to break down any remaining pus.
And if you are unable to do all of this in that hour, make a poultice for the eye with soothing ingredients to alleviate the pain of the eyes, and leave it on for several days until the pain subsides and you are certain there is no danger of abscess; then resume according to the previously described method until it has healed; this is the method of constricting:
of the fistula of the eye
The masters call this type of fistula "arissati"; when you treat it with cautery and hot medicine as I have previously mentioned, but it is not healed, there is a trick to it: you must make an incision on the abscess, at the point where it should burst, and drain all the pus that is in it, until the bone is exposed.
And when the bone is exposed, and you see corruption and blackness, take all the instruments which are in the form described here; and it is called "rough head", and make it of iron one cubit long, and point it like a file as in the present form:
Place the "rough head" on top of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your hands and press down firmly until you feel that the corruption is removed; do this several times, then restore the place with drying medicaments.
If the wound is healed and flesh has grown, and the skin of the wound is healed and remains so for forty days without any inflammation or other adverse event, then know that it is healed; if not, there is no other means but to bring the fistula back to the opening of the bone as follows: reveal the bone a second time with iron, and with moist medicaments, and when it is revealed, take a three-pronged iron pin according to this form, and the head of the pin should be made of iron with three angles, and the shaft should be tapered towards the end as you see here:
Then place the pin next to the bone near the lacrimal duct, and move your hand away from the eye about an inch, then turn the whole pin until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it through the sensation of breath if they keep their hand on their nose; and then restore the place with dry medicaments as I have taught you, and when the flesh grows back and the wound heals, the matter will go to the nose; this is an easier process for the patient.
of the eye socket/orbit dislocation
When the eye is open wide all around and there is no trouble or reduction in vision, then bind the patient; next cauterize, then apply leeches or cups without striking to draw blood, then place a mixture of alum, aloe, incense, and sarcocollex on the eyelid; then bandage the eye and cover it with bandages and soft cloths; take care to use enough soft cloths, doubled in four layers, and apply them gradually according to how much is needed for the eye; next bandage firmly with a hard bandage, and reapply the cups without striking to draw blood; then remove the cups and leave the eye bandaged day and night, and if the mixture softens, tighten the bandage again; then remove the bandage after a day and a night, and if you see that the eye is healing, it is good; if not, reapply the mixture, bandages, and leeches until it heals.
of retinal detachment
When there is a disruption in the retina, it becomes visible and appears as if there are grains of resin on the paper; this is frightening to see. If you view such a detachment, the procedure is to insert a needle into the root of the lower part all the way up to the upper part, then insert another needle with double thread in the corner of the eyelid. Pierce it and leave the first needle as it was placed; next cut off the end of the doubled thread and use it to tie around the edge of the retina, pulling it tight, then remove the needle and place a soft, wet cloth soaked in egg on the eye. Leave it until the threads stick to the retina, then treat the eye with comforting remedies until the wound heals. Sometimes, the wound is restrained by a circle of cloth around the edge of the eye until it has healed.
And if the eye appears swollen, pierce it with a thin spatula that comes from within the eye, and let the watery humor run out, and let the eye descend and go in again; then pull it out until it is healed.
of the swelling of the eye
This disease called "alcunnati" is nothing but a swelling that forms in the eye, similar to descending water, and it is not water; and the manner of appearance of this illness is such that you should have the patient sit on a prepared and upright seat, then hold their head with both hands and move it until you see the swelling come up to your eyes; then let it be punctured and let the light not descend and fall, and let the patient see things as they used to; and if it does not descend, know that it is water, and if the descent of the swelling is not prepared as we have said, then make the patient sit between your hands, then take a thin spatula and insert it through the transparent cornea, along the continuation of the conjunctiva with the cornea and the corona, until the swelling comes out; and when it has come out, distill warm water mixed with honey, or boiled water with fenugreek and honey, into the eye, then cure it with another cure until it is healed.
of the waters (or fluids) of the eye
We have similarities of waters in the division, and that which it is necessary to pierce; and one must work according to health. It is necessary that you make the patient sit between your crossed hands, away from the light of the sun, and bind his good eye very tightly; then place the paper on your left hand if the eye is left, or on your right hand if the eye is right; then take in your right hand, if the eye is left, the instrument which is called "almagda", or in your left hand, if the eye is right; then place the tip of the instrument next to the crown by the size of a grain in that bend of the eye at the side of the smaller tear duct, then push the instrument which is called "almagda" valiantly, and turn your hand until it pierces in the bend of the eye, and feel that almagda comes to the empty space; and it is necessary that the measure of the way almagda be at the depth of the measure of the space which is from the grain to the end of the darkness; and this is the crown of the eye; and you will see the bone in that paper by the clarity of the horned tissue, and then place the instrument until it reaches where the water is, then press it under one way after another. If the water comes down now, let the patient look before him and the instrument in his eye.
After a short rest, and if the water rises in the second duct, apply force with the instrument, and when it is fixed and it no longer rises, then gently remove almagda by turning your hand slightly; and then put in a little bit of gem elixir and raise the eye inside. Then place cotton or wet wool soaked in rose oil and plenty of egg white on top of the eye, and bind it with the good eye. We, and those who are of our time, place a bread poultice with plenty of egg white on top.
And if almagda cannot enter the eye because of its hardness, for there are some men who have very hard eyes, then it is necessary that you take the instrument which is called "alberit", whose shape is as follows:
And perforate the conjunctiva only, and do not go too deep, but make a subtle hole, then place almagda as we have said; and at the completion of the work prepare for the patient a comfortable sleeping aid, in which he may sleep on his back in a dark room; and be free from all movements, and eat light foods, and do not move his head to left or right, and bind him according to his condition until three days have passed; then unbind him in that same dark room, and test his sight, and let him see some things, and then replace the binding for seven days; and it is necessary that you do not do this during the hour of the cure or after the incision now, but rather lighten this, so that the water may rise quickly.
if pustules occur, that you unbind the eye before the seventh day, and direct it towards the one who soothes swellings; and when it has calmed down, then loosen the vision and place a bandage on its edge for a few days, and let him always remain in that dark room. And then leave the house rarely and briefly, and turn your attention to your duties; and know that no disciples should intervene in this case.
And a man came to us who was from Yrach, who told us that in their country they make almagda perciet, which one can suck the water (juice) from, but nonetheless I have never seen any such thing in our land, nor do I read of it in books of ancient knowledge; and perhaps it is a new thing.
And these are the appearances of the forms of almagda, so that those who do not know it may see (them); and they should be made of pure tin:
And let the tops of them be of this same delicacy, and the rear parts in three sharp points.[translating "agues" as "sharp points"]
of the flesh near the nose
Sometimes different kinds of flesh are born near the nose, some of which resemble scorpions with many feet; and there are such where the flesh is swollen and of a foxy color, and others that have soft flesh of good color. In this case of these flesh growths that are soft, but not swollen, you should make the patient sit between your hands in front of the sun; clear their nostrils, and apply the instrument to those flesh growths, and pull them out; then cut what you can hold with a sharp, thin spatula on one side, until you know that the flesh has been completely removed.
And if there remains any part that cannot be cut, open it with all one instrument very delicately and lightly, so that nothing remains; and if pus forms or an abscess arises, treat it as appropriate; and if they are malignant abscesses, hurry and cauterize them until the blood stops and all the flesh growths are removed, then pour vinegar or sterilized water into the nose.
If the nose does not open and moisture reaches the palate, know that it is healed; and if the moisture does not break through as it should, know that flesh has grown in the bone above, which the instrument cannot reach. In this case, you should insert a fairly thick linen thread, with small knots at regular intervals (about the width of a fingernail or less), and place the patient's head with the thread in its nostril to the best of their ability, and pull gently while sniffing until the thread comes out of the nose into the mouth. Many children do this in school, and it is an easy task for those who wish to do it. Then hold the part of the nose that comes out through the nose with one hand, and the other end that comes out of the mouth with the other hand, and feel your way along the knots until you know that they have become embedded in the flesh. When you are sure that the knots have lodged in the flesh, pull out the thread gently, wipe away the blood, and moisten the thread with Egyptian ointment before reinserting it into the nose as before. Do this for three days or more, until the ointment dissolves all remaining flesh. Then insert a piece of plastic tubing into the nose for several days until it heals, and use drying medicines if necessary. This is the method of using the instrument to purge the head, which is used to distill oils and medicines into the nose.
And it should be of silver or brass, resembling an open lamp, such as a candle, and the wick similarly; and if you wish, make a closed candle, and let the instrument be full to purge the head; and have a handle on the head to hold it when heating the oil or any liquid.
of flesh from the nose
Often arises in the head of the nose a disease called "telul", and it grows and becomes large at times, to the point where it is visible; and therefore, you must cut it at the beginning and remove it all, then place the cautery or hot medicine on the wound; and if you delay cutting it until it has grown, see if it is hard, of purple color, with poor sensation: do not touch it with iron because it is an abscess that has festered, because when it is cut even once, great harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is soft to the touch, not of purple color, and you see that you can cut all of it, empty the patient and cut the wound without fear, and cure it with drying and constricting things.
when the nose has been cut and sewn[References:
Know that when solutions of continuity come to one of these cartilaginous works, it profits little, except in some men. Therefore, when this happens to someone, look if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then approximate the two lips to a suture, then cure it until it heals; and if the lips are already separated on one side and the other, you must scarify all the edges of their wound until they heal, then approximate the two lips to a suture and bind them, and put powder of dragon's blood and ground incense on it, and place on top of the powders a piece of strong plaster or another binding plaster, and leave it until it comes off by itself, then cure it with an ointment until it heals.
The manner of suturing is such that you approximate the wound: either with needles, as we have said in the suture of the belly; or with thread, as I have made known to you.
abscesses of the lips
To some men, hard abscesses like grains of pepper appear within the lips, smaller and larger; then you must turn the lips, and make an incision on each node, and take it with forceps and cut each part; then apply a poultice of powdered vitriol after the incision until the blood is stopped; and then apply goose grease, and cure the wound with dry things until it heals.
of the flesh of the gums
Often, a hardened flesh is born on the gums, which the ancients called "albulus"; you should hold it with tongs and cut at its root, letting the pus or blood flow; then put vitriol powder or other restraining and desiccative powders on the wound; and if this flesh comes back after the incision, which often happens, cut it again and cauterize it: it will not come back after cauterization; and these are the shapes of the instruments for cutting.
of abscesses or inflammations. The term "sordes" in medieval medical texts often refers to purulent, infected matter or discharges that accumulate in the body and need to be drained or cleaned out. So "des sordens" could refer to the treatment or removal of such abscesses or inflamed areas.
Sometimes, hard and rough crusts form on the top of teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, which are ugly and harsh; and sometimes the teeth become black, yellow, or green, such that corruption reaches the gum, and the teeth become foul-smelling; you must make the patient sit between your hands, with their head in your lap, and scrape off any visible tartar, crusts, or stains from the teeth until nothing remains; and do the same for black, green, yellow, and other stains until they are cleaned; and if all of the buildup is removed during the first cleaning, that is good; if not, resume cleaning on the second and third days until everything is removed; and know that teeth require various shapes of instruments to clean them, depending on what the task requires, because scrapers used to clean between teeth have different forms than those used to clean the surfaces of teeth; and make sure you have these shapes and others prepared.
It is necessary, when you cure the tooth of its pain, that you delay pulling it as long as you can, because one should not do this hastily; for it is a very serious matter up to the point where there is no excuse for damaging it. Then, when the patient is constrained to have it pulled, you must make sure of the tooth that is causing pain. Often times, the pain leaves the patient and they think it's gone, but it persists despite pulling the good tooth; this we have often seen done by quack dentists. And when you are certain of the tooth causing pain, you must sear around the tooth with a strong styptic to protect the gum all around; then pull it with your hands or fine pliers at first tug and tug until it is well loosened, then securely fasten the pliers; and have the patient's head in your lap and hold it still so that it does not move.
After pulling the tooth out straight without breaking it, and if it does not come out easily, take one of these instruments and gently push it in on both sides, and move it as you did before. And if the tooth is pierced and decayed, you must fill it with cloth where the holes are; and carefully pull it with pliers so that it does not break while pulling, and you must work very delicately around the gum to loosen the tooth.
And take good care not to break it and leave a part in the patient's jaw, which will cause greater pains than the first due to the malice of the root. And be careful not to act like ignorant dentists who sometimes out of haste and recklessness break the tooth socket and do not treat it as we have mentioned; instead they bring about great illness because of the roots that remain or because of the broken tooth, which we have often seen. And when the tooth is pulled, rinse the socket with wine or vinegar and salt; and if bleeding occurs, which often happens, fill the socket with powdered vitriol; and if this does not work, cauterize it.
The shapes of the instruments with which one moves the teeth first should be long and have thick handles, so that they do not bend when you pull the tooth; and these are the shapes:
And they should have thick shanks so that they do not bend when pulled, and they should be made of good iron, and serrated to hold teeth in place.
on the roots of the teeth When the root remains to be pulled, then you should place cotton soaked in butter on the spot for one or two days until the gums are softened. Then use tongs called "algefri," which have a shape like a bird's beak; and they should be made with a lime-like texture, and this is their shape:[ST1] It is not clear what is meant by "and c’est li forme" in the original text. I translated it as "and this is their shape," but it could also mean "and that is the shape" or something similar.
And if the roots do not want to come out with all of these tongs, then you must cut open the flesh all around the root and place in it the instrument called "althali," that is, a scalpel, of which this is the shape:[ST1] It is not clear what is meant by "c’est a savoir palainche" in the original text. I translated it as "that is, a scalpel," but it could also mean "namely, a scalpel" or something similar.
And let it be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the roots come out through this, that is good; if not, use all the instruments, of which forms are described later.
And one can help themselves with this instrument that has two handles, of which this is the form:
and other iron instruments that are in front of the teeth's root, and of this instrument that looks like large pliers, of which this is the form:
And let these instruments be strong so that they do not break, and know that there are many dental instruments; and also other instruments that are not mentioned here; and the wise master subtly finds his own instrument, according to what his work and the disease show him, because there are such diseases for which the ancients did not teach any instrument due to their diversity; and one does not break the cart or other bones, where it will rot, but instead searches among the instruments that are needed, as I have told you, and helps with gestures, of which this is the form: And let them be thick and able to hold the bone so that it does not splinter, but can instead hold and remove it; and then restore the place with medicines appropriate for this, and if there is rotting in the bone, and it is small, then use all of this instrument for it.
When the tooth appears not in accordance with the body's natural form, and its shape is ugly, and the same is true for young women, you should determine if the tooth is new after the tooth, and it is not in the right place, and it cannot be straightened or filed: then file it; but if it is crooked compared to the other tooth, take this tool, the shape of which is shown here, similar to a small beak, and made of sharp iron:
And hold the instrument close and keep it in your hands for several days due to the tooth's hardness, and so that you do not move the other teeth, and if it appears that it can be filed down, file it with a file like the one shown here in form:
and it is similar to the file used to make needles; and carefully and lightly file down the tooth, holding it still until it is loose; then use a plane at the end for smoothing, and if the tooth is too sharp and cuts the tongue, file down the roughness until it is even, so that it does not cut the tongue or distort speech.
when the tooth loosens.
When the front teeth loosen, either from a blow or a fall, and the patient cannot chew food without defecating, and you have treated them with constricting medicines to no avail; then they must be constricted with a gold wire, for silver wire turns green and rots, but gold never changes; and let the wire be of medium thickness, not too thick or too thin, according to the space between the teeth; and if you wish to realign the teeth, take the filament and place it double between the two healthy teeth, then place the loose teeth between the loose teeth, whether there is one or more, until you come to a healthy tooth on the other side; then begin covering again from where you started, and gently but firmly pull your hand until it does not move; and let your grip be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape. Then cut the ends of the wire with pliers and align them, and place them between the healthy tooth and the loose tooth, and position them so as not to injure the tongue; and then leave them tightly in place as long as they can endure, and if they loosen or the wire breaks, then constrict it with another wire; if they remain and function in this way for their entire duration, this is the method for realigning two healthy teeth and two loose teeth, as you can see.
And when a tooth falls out, it is replaced in its place, as we have said, as fresh as possible; and let no one who is not wise and skilled interfere; and sometimes the shape of a tooth is made from animal bone, and it is placed in the empty socket and constricted as we have said, and it remains and serves for a long time.
to cut the tie of the tongue.
Sometimes there is a ligament under the tongue that is natural at birth or occurs accidentally due to a healed wound; and the procedure is as follows: open the patient's mouth and hold their head, then lift the tongue and cut the nervous ligament widely, so that the tongue is loosened from its anchorage. And if there is hardness or a knot due to the healing of a wound, insert the hook and cut the ligament widely; and make sure not to cut too deep, as the artery is beneath it. When you have finished, apply a little rose-colored or cold water, then place a linen bandage underneath the tongue. Have the patient hold this in their mouth every night so that the ligament does not heal again. If bleeding occurs, apply vitriol powder to it; and if the wound becomes infected, cauterize it with a slow-burning cautery, which is good for this purpose; then continue treating it until it heals.
And if you see it of a bluish-black or hard color, so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it at all, for it is a chancre; and if it is declining towards blenchor, and there is moisture, then place the "oncine" (a medical instrument) and make an incision with a thin spatula, and release it from one side and the other; and if the blood comes to meet your work, then apply vinegar powder until it stops bleeding, then return to your work until you draw everything out; then lift it up with ease and support, and cure it with other cures until it is healed.
of abscesses in the throat
Sometimes there come within the throat growths that are called "godath," and they are properly called the "two almonds." And when you cure them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, beware: if it is an abscess of hard consistency and bluish color, then do not touch it at all with iron. And if it is red and the root is large, then do not touch it at all with iron, so as not to cause bleeding; but leave it until it has ripened, and then you will open it, or it will break open by itself; and if it is of white color and swollen, and the root is thin, then have your instrument ready to cover (it), but first look to see if the hard swelling is at rest and calm. Then have the patient sit facing the sun, and his head should be in your lap, and open his mouth and take it with his hands, and press down the tongue beneath the entire instrument, of which this is the form; and it should be of silver or fine brass as a scalpel:
And when you press the tongue down with all this instrument and see the abscess, then take the "oncine" (a medical instrument) and insert it into the almond (growth), and draw it out as much as you can; and draw some of the pus with it, then cover it with the instrument, which has the form of forceps; and yet the cheeks are curved inward towards each other and are very sharp, and it is made of iron or steel.
And if you don't have this tool at hand, take tongs instead, of which this is the shape:
And let one side be sharp and the other blunt; and once you have bent one of the almond-shaped parts, bend the other in the same manner; and after the incision, gargle the patient with warm water and vinegar; and if there is an evacuation of blood, gargle the patient with water or the skins of pomegranates cooked, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the bleeding stops; then treat it until it has healed; and sometimes other abscesses appear in the throat besides the two almond-shaped parts, so cut them in the same way as the two almond-shaped parts.
And I treated a woman for an abscess in her throat, which was quite large and had closed up her entire throat, such that the woman could not breathe through the passage that was blocked, nor could she eat or drink, and she would have died if she remained like that for one or two days. The abscess was so large that it had pushed out two veins through the two nostrils. I acted quickly and inserted a probe into one of the nostrils, then pulled it out and extracted a large quantity of pus; I did the same thing in the other nostril, opened her mouth and pressed on her tongue; then I inserted the probe into these abscesses and cut into one part, and only a small amount of blood came out; and thus the passage in the woman's throat was unblocked, and she began to drink water and then wine, and I continued to cut into this abscess for a long time; and the abscess grew larger again and filled up the space that I had emptied, becoming very large; then I applied pressure and cauterized it inside her throat: thus it stopped growing; and I left from there, not knowing what God did with her after I left.
of the eye (uvea)
When pus descends to the eye, and it is swollen and elongated, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is below, large and round, it is called "eye". When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, and you see that the chief abscess has calmed down, and it is fine, then it is necessary to make an incision; and the one that is rounded assembled and not long; and it is sanguine or of a fleshy color or black, then it is necessary to avoid making an incision in it. Because there is great danger for the patient. Therefore, when you see it, according to its swelling and length, you should have the patient sit facing the sun, and press their tongue with the instrument that we have mentioned before; then insert the probe into the eye and pull it down, and cut along one of the two edges that I have said in the incision of the two almonds. And it is necessary to not cut further than the excess that is beyond the natural limit; because if you cut more, it harms the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and treat it until it is healed. And if the patient is afraid of cutting, then it is necessary to use a trick with cauterization without fear. And the method of cautery is sharp and pointed. And it is that the patient places their head on your shoulder, and then presses their tongue with the instrument that we have mentioned in the chapter of cautery, and apply live coals, so that they are not too thick nor too thin; and use the handle of this instrument, of which this is the shape:
And have the patient have a hair on their head, or place the medicine in it, such as the teeth of a spoon, and place the instrument full of medicine on the eye; and let the patient lie on their side, so that the saliva and mucus flow from their mouth with the medicine inside, so that it does not descend to the throat and cause harm; then keep your hand on all the medicine and press it on the eye, for the duration of half an hour, until you see it absorbed and the irritation of the medicine has calmed down; and if necessary, take cotton and wrap it around some instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and insert the instrument full of cotton into the wound above, until the cotton hardens on the eye; and do this often, until the cautery is complete, then let it dry and fall off after three or five days. And if you need to reapply the cautery of the medicine, then do so, and after the cautery, clean around the eye with a cotton swab dipped in butter, and clean what is around the medicine; and rinse with cold water, and cure with gargles until it is healed.
This cure is safer than incision or cauterization; if it is treated with fumigation in this manner, take pennyroyal and hyssop and oregano and rue and chamomile and elderberry and similar herbs, and combine them all or some of them in one pot, and place a spout on it; and let the pot be well glued with strong earth, and in the middle of the pot there should be an instrument like this: And whether it is of silver or bronze, and one of the eyes should be placed in the patient's mouth until the vapor rises to the eye through the temple, until the eye becomes mortified; then reapply it frequently, until the eye dries out, and make sure not to do this at the beginning of the hot abscess, for many things can happen; and do not do it at all except at the decline of a hot abscess. And if this instrument is not present, take a tube and put an eggshell in the patient's head, so that the mouth of the patient is not too hot; for the eggshell does not allow the vapor to overwhelm the mouth, and it is a good remedy altogether healthy.
Often a bone or fish spine, or some other object gets stuck in the throat, it is then necessary to remove what you can see, and press the patient's tongue against the sun with all the instrument, so that you may see the object move; and what does not appear to you and is embedded in the throat, it is necessary to make the patient vomit after food has been cooked in the stomach; perhaps the object will come out through vomiting; or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of thread, or a lettuce root, or a piece of dry bread; and tie a thread to the sponge and swallow it; and when it reaches the place, it will become stiff, and then you can pull it out; and if it does not come out by what we have said, take an instrument made of wood in this form:
And let the instrument be curved at the end so that it can enter more easily into the throat, and hold the head high; and take care not to touch the epiglottis, nor force the bone in; and it is better if the patient inserts the instrument themselves, so that they know where the object is; they insert it downwards, or pull it out with the entire instrument evenly, until it is removed.
of the throat sinus
Sometimes the vein is treated, as I have said in the division, by medical cure; and when this does not help at all, then look in the sick person's throat in the sun, after pressing their tongue with the instrument that I have told you. And if you see the vein, then pull it with a tiny hook, or with delicate tweezers worth for this. And if this is not valuable, then take a bladder leaf, and put it in the sick person's throat, then put a hot iron on the tip of the bladder. And do this often. And if the patient becomes thirsty all day, then take a full glass of cold water, and open the mouth, and throw it in without swallowing, and move it with their hand often; and as soon as the vein feels the water, it will fall.
And if it does not fall as we have said, then fumigate the patient with asafetida, with the instrument that I have mentioned in the fumigation of the eye; do this many times, for it will fall without delay. And the manner of fumigation is as follows: take a pot in which there are hot coals, and cover it with a pierced cloth, and in this hole put the opening of the instrument; then throw your fumigation, and the patient puts the end of the bladder in their mouth, and closes their mouth so that the smoke does not escape, but reaches the vein; and the vein will fall now, and if it does not fall, then repeat the fumigation many times; and let the patient suffer thirst, and eat salty and bitter things, and do not drink water; and then it will be necessary for it to come out by this method.
And the shape of the instrument with which to treat the vein, when it can be seen, is similar to curved pliers so as to easily enter the throat; and it should resemble the beak of a bird of prey, and have roughness like sandpaper, so that what it takes, it cannot release; and see here its shape:
The chapter on abscesses.
Many similarities of abscess exist, according to what the following remembrance brings in this book, one after the other, and they are different in perforation and size; and it is in two ways, one of which is in its own likeness, and those that retain moisture. And the second manner is according to the locations where they are in the body. For the abscesses of the head are different than those of the base, and the abscesses of the fleshy part are different than those that come in joints, and each one must be judged in the work.
And there are abscesses that should not be pierced until the boil is dead according to its completion; and there are such as must be pierced when they have grown, and do not die according to their completion, such as abscesses that are near joints. For when abscesses come near joints, and one leaves it until it is completely rotten, perhaps the ligaments and nerves of the joint have been corrupted, which causes contraction in that member. Or the abscess is near the principal member, and if you delay the piercing until it is dead, it will harm the principal member; or it is near the base, so one must pierce it when it is dead; and one should not pierce an abscess that has grown without digestion completed, except for those that are near the base, lest it rots inside and becomes elongated, forming a fistula; and cannot heal in a long time.
And it is necessary that you know the hour of piercing the abscess when it is dead according to its completion, and this is when the pain has subsided, and the cessation of fever, and the decrease of pain and redness, and the softening and swelling of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and you must make the incision in the lowest part of the abscess, where it is most prominent; and let the incision be long enough for the body, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in joints, and near nerves and arteries, and on all sides where there is no curvature.
And in those that are curved, according to the curvature of the member. And when an abscess is in the fleshy part, it is better to leave the incision until it has solidified after digestion is completed, as we have said. For if you pierce it before then, the body's fluid will be elongated and full of filth; and perhaps the lips and depths of it will harden. And there are some abscesses that are pierced according to the width of the body, depending on the need of the member. And in small abscesses, make small incisions; and in large abscesses, large incisions, and many splits according to the likeness of the size of the abscess; and there are such abscesses where it is necessary to cut out the core and cover it. When it has become as one cloth, and has died, then do the same as with tumors: and there are some that are split into three angles, and there are some that are cut like a myrtle leaf, such as abscesses of the glands; and there are some where a round incision is made, and other shapes and similar cuts.
Those who have no visible abscesses, such as a soft superficial abscess, it is necessary to fully pierce them; and it is necessary, when the abscess is large and has gathered great pus, and you pierce it, not to draw out all the pus in that hour, but only some of it; then stop up the abscess until the next day, and then draw out some more; do this many times, gradually, until all the pus comes out; do the same even if the patient is of weak vitality, such as women, young children, old decrepit men. For the spirit sometimes jumps when the pus is coming out, causing the patient to suddenly die, and you would not realize it. Therefore, be very cautious in this matter and, once you have pierced your abscess, clean the wound and check if the abscess wound is small; and if it is a flat cut, then apply tension bands of linen or old cotton; and if it is large abscesses with many holes, then it is necessary to place a tent in each one so that they come together; and if you have cut off a piece of the skin in the abscess and turned it over, then it is necessary to fill it with old linen rags or linen cloth without moisture, and bind it for three days; then remove it and dress the wound with ointment until it heals.
And if bleeding occurs during your work, apply cold water and a damp cloth to the area multiple times. If the bleeding persists, provide care and treatment, using the powders that I have mentioned in this book, and if it is winter and the location of the abscess is very sensitive, then place tents and damp cloths soaked in wine and warm oil on top; and if it is summer and the area is fleshy, then apply damp cloths soaked in water and oil, or wine and cold oil, for three days as we have said; and then loosen the abscess and clean and dress it as needed until it heals.
And this is what must be universally known in the treatment of abscesses: I have told you how to proceed with the treatment of abscesses, and here is the chapter.

"Scrofula" is a medical term used to describe a group of diseases characterized by the presence of swollen lymph nodes, typically in the neck. The term comes from the Latin word "scrofa," which means "she-pig," likely because the affected lymph nodes can resemble the swollen glands of a pig. Scrofula is also known as "the king's evil" because it was once believed that the touch of a king or queen could cure the disease. This belief dates back to the time of King Edward the Confessor in England and was continued by subsequent monarchs. However, this practice has been abandoned and there is no scientific evidence to support the idea that royal touch can cure scrofula. Scrofula is usually treated with antibiotics, but surgical removal of the affected lymph nodes may be necessary in some cases.
"Scrofula" often occurs in the neck, under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes appear in other parts of the body, and are connected to each other. Each scrofula is specifically located in its own node, like the knots and abscesses on the head, as we have said; and there are many different kinds of scrofula. Some contain moisture, while others are malignant and do not want to submit to treatment. In this case, if you see a scrofula with good disposition and similar in color to the skin, and it is not swollen in the nerves of the neck or arteries or ducts, and is not deep, then you should cut it open from above, and skin around it on all sides, and pull out the two lips of the wound as needed with your fingers, just as we have said for abscesses of the head; and remove little by little, making sure not to cut nerves or veins, and that the scalpel is neither too sharp nor cutting, so that you do not cut what you should not.
And if you cut a vein or artery, and it does not let you work, put in the wound vitriol powder, or any powders that stop blood and constrict the wound; and leave it until the abscess has calmed down, and the wound has softened and begun to rot. And when the bleeding has stopped, return to your work, until you have completed it; then see with your skilled judgment if there remain any small scrofulous patches, and cut and clean them. And if there is a large vein at the root of the scrofulous patch, it is not appropriate to cut that scrofulous patch at its root, but bind it with a double strong thread and let it fall off by itself, without harm; then fill the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then cure.
And if you cut all of the scrofulous patch, it is necessary to bring together the two lips of the wound and sew it now, so that there is no remaining excess due to the size of the scrofulous patch. It is necessary to focus on cutting the root of it and pulling it out, and sewing it as we have said. Those scrofulous patches that have an accumulation, pierce them where it is clear; and pierce it as was said before, depending (on the location), then apply tents with ointment and similar things, so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, cure it with a running ointment, until the flesh is healed.

of the chancre
We have said in the division the similarities of chancre, and how one should work on it with medicines, and how to avoid the cure of iron; and we say that the chancre swells in the groin, and requires great caution in its treatment. And the ancients said that when a chancre is in a place where it can be scraped, such as a chancre that is on the breasts, or on the thigh, and similar places, one must completely remove it when it first appears. And when it becomes large and old, one should not approach it at all, for I have never cured any; nor has anyone ever cured any before me.

Because I have seen that most masters and surgeons who performed circumcision around one thumb's width and with force, using a novacule, avoided the area because there are two layers there, and perhaps they cut the one above and leave the one below.

"from the stone" (in this context, likely referring to a kidney or bladder stone that is being treated with the enema)
We have previously said in the division the kinds of stones, and the extraction together with their medicines; and I have said the difference between the stone stuck in the kidneys, and all the signs, and in what kind of stone one should work by cutting; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell it to you plainly and concisely.
I say that the stone which is stuck in the bladder happens more often in children, and this is a sign that the water jumps from the bladder similarly to water in its subtlety; and it appears sandy, and the patient urinates with difficulty, and urinates frequently, and then becomes rigid; and there are many of these jumps; and the foundation is light in children until they reach 4 years old, and it is very grievous in the elderly, and it is moderate in those who are between youth and old age; and the treatment is easier for those who have large stones, than for those who have small ones.
And when it comes to the treatment, first, it is necessary to cleanse the patient with an enema, to remove all the filth that is in the intestines. For it often interferes with finding the stone.[br] (Note: The word "clistere" refers to an enema.)
Then, lift the patient by the feet and straighten them out, moving them downwards, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder and protrudes somewhat outside; then make the patient sit between your hands, ready, and let their hands be under their thighs, so that the bladder is completely lowered; then search for it and touch it inside;
if you feel the stone in the area, hurry to cut into the stone. And if it does not fall at the first touch, moisten your index finger with oil from your left hand, if the patient is elderly, or your middle finger if the patient is a mature adult; and insert it into its foundation, and search for the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, pull it towards the bladder neck; then press upon it with your finger, and remove it to the side where you intend to make the incision.
And command the assistant to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to lift the hips with his right hand and remove the skin beneath the hips on the side where the incision is made; then insert the spatula, which has the following shape:
And make the incision between the area of the hips and the perineum, not in the middle but near the left testicle; and let it be directly above the stone, and your hands should be placed firmly on the perineum, and let the width of the incision be greater at the outside than the inside, and adjusted according to the size of the stone, not too large.
Perhaps the pressure of the hands on the perineum will cause the stone to come out easily without effort; and be aware that some stones have angles and sharp edges, making them difficult to extract; while others are softer, similar to a gland, and round, which makes it easy to extract.
To the one with angles and edges, make the incision larger; and if it does not break open, you should pull on pincers that are like a file at the tip, to extract the stone so that it doesn't shatter; or you place under it a thin curved instrument at the tip; and if you can't trick it in this way, widen the opening a little more, and if the flesh closes up again, constrict it with vitriol.
And if there are multiple stones, place the largest one at the neck of the bladder first, then cut on top and extract it, and then the smaller ones if there are more. And if they are very large, they must be smoothed out, and a larger incision must be made. For two things can happen to the patient: either they die or urine constantly comes out through the opening that the flesh cannot close; but still try to extract it, or break it apart with pincers, as much as you can remove it in pieces.
And when you have completed your work, apply the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and bind it, and place a damp cloth soaked in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water, on top to calm the hot abscess; then raise the patient up by their neck and do not loosen the binding until the third day.
And when you unbind it, rinse the area well with oil and water, then clean it with a diaphoretic ointment and a basilicon ointment until it is healed.
And if abscesses or ulcers come in the wound and congealed blood in the bladder, and urine is retained, which is known to happen without pain with urination: then put your finger in the wound and extract that blood, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder and cause it to rot.
Then raise the wound of water, pus, and decay, and help it in all ways that you know, until it is healed; and it is necessary that during all the times that you care for it, you bind its two thighs together and apply the medicines to the affected area.
And if the stone is small and it is in the urethra and lodged in there, and urine cannot exit: then care for it as I have said before, cut it many times, it is excused from cutting for this treatment. I have proven this myself.
Take an iron fork of this shape and make it with three sharp points on one handle.
then take a thread and tie it around the rod beneath the stone, so that it cannot move back into the bladder; then gently insert the probe into the rod until it reaches the stone; and turn the probe with your hand in the stone repeatedly, as much as you can, until you can pierce the stone from the other side; soon urine will flow, then press your hand on what remains of the stone that is inside the rod. It will break immediately and exit along with the urine, and the patient will be healed.
And if you cannot do this because of some hindrance, then tie a thread beneath the stone and another above it; then make an incision in the rod towards the stone between the two ties, then remove it and untie the tie, and clean the congealed blood that is in the wound; and cure it until it is healed.
of the female stone (i.e., a calculus or concretion in the female urinary tract)
It rarely happens that a stone is inserted in women, and if it does happen, the cure is difficult and hindered by three things: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a skilled midwife who can examine her, even when she is chaste.

of castration
Know that castration is forbidden in our religion, and therefore I would not like to speak of it in this book; and it is not necessary except for two reasons: one is so that the physician may know how to respond when asked about it, and how to perform the procedure; and the other reason is because we often need to castrate certain animals to assist us, such as goats, sheep, pigs, and other beasts. I say then that castration is performed in two ways: either by attraction or by cutting. In the one done by attraction, we make the animal sit in hot water until the groin is softened and relaxed; then pull on it with your hand until it is back in place and you no longer feel resistance. Regarding surgical castration: one must tie down the animal and press the skin of the groin with your left hand, then tie the suspensory ligament and make one cut on each testicle after they have been properly prepared; leave some of the sheath and the delicate sheath that is above the vessels; this method of castration is more reliable than the one done by attraction because in the latter there may be some tissue left behind from the groin, causing the animal to still desire lust; then clean and care for the wound until it heals.

Des hemorroides (of hemorrhoids)
Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that are not usually visible, and when hemorrhoids become old, they turn into piles; and we have previously mentioned their likenesses, and signs, and I will say here those that receive treatment. of childbirth
It is necessary for the midwife to first recognize the natural form of childbirth and its signs, which are as follows: when you see a woman pushing downwards and craving strong smells, then know that this birth is in accordance with the natural form, and the baby's position is under its head and the afterbirth is with it. And when you see these signs, then gently press on her stomach so that the baby comes out quickly, for as soon as it rests on its head, the afterbirth comes out with it and the woman is cleansed of her excess by good purification. But if it comes any other way, then it does not come naturally. For sometimes it comes with its feet first, or outside the body, or the hands, or it comes up to the stomach, or turns around to the neck, and in other bad positions. of wounds
We have previously spoken in the division about wound treatment; now we will tell you of hand and medical treatments, according to their completion.
I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and by what they are made.
The things by which wounds are made are by striking with a stone, cutting with a sword and knife, or a spear or stick or arrow, or similar things.
Or wounds are made according to the parts of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or the head, or the chest, or the belly, or the liver, and similar limbs.[IST] Ou selonc la matiere de quoi il est faites; si com plaie de feu ou de poison.
And I will tell you the treatment for each wound, and I will begin with simple head wounds, for reminders will come in their own chapter.
I say that when a simple wound comes to the head and the bone is not broken, pay attention if it is from striking by a stone or similar things, and the skin is still torn and the wound is large. And if you suspect a hot abscess: then cause it to drain immediately from the head itself if blood is oozing from the wound, and let the discharge be on the side opposite the injured part.
And avoid giving the patient rich food and meat.

and place cotton soaked in rose oil only, or in styptic wine, on the wound if abscesses are prone to form;

And if you find rotting flesh on the skin, and it is not attached to the bone, then cut away all the decayed flesh and discard it, then cure the wound.
And if there is an artery in the wound or a vein that cannot be stopped with medicine, then tie off the artery, and if you find it loose, bind it with a thread. And if that does not help, then cauterize it.
And if these wounds are small and simple, the cure is easy: and that is to apply this powder which solidifies once the wound has moved (i.e., been cleaned).
And the manner of making the powder is as follows: take one part incense, two parts dragon's blood, three parts quicklime, and finely grind (the ingredients) into a powder. and apply the powder to the wound, and bind it firmly until it dries out completely and becomes one with all its blood.[Original text implies that the application of the powder will dry the wound out and help in joining the skin together.]
And then bind it well and leave it alone without loosening, if there is no swelling; for the medicine should not be removed until it has healed.[In this context, "madicine" refers to the powder and any dressings used to hold it in place.]
Sometimes, quicklime is used alone if incense and dragon's blood are not available, but only after the wound has been cleaned by the practitioner.
And if the wound has moved (shifted) itself, it should be left as is, and this powder should not be applied at all.
but apply some digestive ointments, or poultices made of barley flour with water and honey, until it (the wound) dries up. then continue to treat the wound with other treatments until it is healed.

and it is a small worm that is born between the skin and flesh, and moves throughout the body going up and down, and it can be felt well as it moves from one limb to another, for it breaks the skin where it goes and comes out.

Of arrows
Arrows are diverse, according to their likenesses and according to the parts of the body where they land.
The diversity of arrows is such that there are some with large points, some with small ones, some barbed, and some blunt;[ Bastard arrows (chevees) have a hardened tip but no sharp point. ] and of those which have two angles, and of those which have tongues, and of those which have fragments; and that which falls in any limb falls in two ways: when it falls in the principal part,

Here begins the book of fractures.
This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it concerns the restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Know, dear son, that foolish surgeons who ignore this chapter have never seen any of the ancient books, nor have they read (them).
And because of this, the knowledge is strange in our land, for I never found anyone skilled in it.
And I know nothing about it, except through the knowledge of ancient books, in which I have studied so much that I have become proficient in it, and also through experience and habit from my life.
And I have described for you in this chapter what it contains, and summarized it at the end, and clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are prepared, just as I did in the two chapters preceding this one.
Then it is necessary that we say in the prologue of this book the summaries of the words and the chapters where the wise man directs his attention, and remains on the truth, so that those who are proven may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
I say that when a fracture or dislocation or twisting or crushing comes to someone, then it is necessary to quickly heal the patient from one side and the other, if nothing prevents you, such as weakness of the body, children, or the elderly;
or if the time is not very hot or too cold; and eat only lean foods, that is to say cold games such as bird and hare meat, and do not drink wine, nor eat any fatty meats, and do not fill yourself with food which fills the veins with blood, until you are certain that there is no danger of a hot abscess or spreading of matter in the limb; so let the patient return to their original diet and regimen that they were used to.
And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary to nourish the patient with foods that make for thick nutrition, or have a viscous quality, such as wheat cooked in water, and rice, and heads, and feet, and tripe of cattle, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things. For at times, during the setting, movement and healing are sped up and the fracture occurs more quickly.

And if the patient is wounded by the shards of arrows after being tightened in a healthy place, place under them plugs of linen, or wool padding, so that they do not wound themselves.
When the wound is accompanied by a break and the flesh is torn, I will tell you the cure after this.
And know that it is not appropriate to bind all broken limbs with arrows on the first day.[_](id:r86v2o3aokvp) Because when the limb is large, arrows should not be applied until after 5 or 7 days, or more depending on the certainty of a hot abscess appearing.
And here is the method for ancient poultices to heal fractures, dislocations, and twists: take flour that clings to the walls of a mill, and thicken it with plenty of egg, and apply this mixture, not too clear nor too thick, and use it. This is the common way of the poultice that restores fracture in many ways, and also for women and small children, because it is neither too hot nor too cold.[_](id:r86v2o3aokvp)
Another manner of plaster restores the fracture and dislocation and twisted limb: take three ounces each of alabaster, ladanum, enula campana, asafetida, and gum arabic, and myrrh and aloes, five ounces each; aloe juice, eight ounces; and reduce to a powder, and mix with egg white; if the complexion of the person is hot, use this plaster, for it is of good composition, and quickly restores broken bones, and is beneficial for many men.
Another plaster that is good for twisted limbs: take myrrh and plantain, ten ounces; myrrh and aloes, eight ounces; acacia, six ounces; Armenian bole, ten ounces, and grind well, and infuse with water or egg white, and administer.
Another manner of plaster for dislocated joints and bones out of their places, and eases the pain that occurs, and is used by surgeons for cutting bone and fractures: take new wool, and moisten it with vinegar and cooked oil, and place on the affected area. This plaster does not heal completely, but it is good for relieving hot abscesses, and removing pain properly.
Another plaster that restores broken bones: take dried fig leaves and crushed clover, grind together, and make a plaster. (Note: spelling, measurements, and some plant names have been modernized)
Another way of applying a plaster for the healing of bone fractures and to reduce the remaining abscess. Take root of marshmallow, chamomile, violet flowers, flour of bran, of each one part; and grind, and make into a paste with wine, and if the limb is heated, mix it with moist coriander water or plain water, and use it.
Another stronger way of applying a plaster, compared to the first one, when hard abscess comes to the restoration of the limb. Take roots of marshmallow, flax seeds, valerian, melilot, and elderflower and violet and chamomile flowers, of all take an equal amount; and grind, and make into a paste with salty water or plain water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb, and its rest.
Hippocrates states in his book that one should not place any plaster on a broken limb to restore it but only a cerate made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and he says that it should be moderately warm and not too hard or too soft.
And it seems that Galen also recommends that one should apply to a broken limb, for the purpose of restoring it, mildly warm dry substances such as myrrh, aloe and incense, as we have said.
Another manner of plaster that is useful for wound and pain: take a beetle and chopped off human hair or bird feathers, and red lead, and boil evenly, and grind, and make it into a plaster and apply it.
And then loosen it a little afterwards, and make sure that the patient does not feel any pain, and that the bone has not moved from its place; if so, do not loosen it for many days.
And if pain comes to the place, or itching, without rest or swelling, then hurry and loosen it, and remove the plaster immediately; and take a light cloth and sea sponge, soaked in water, and lift the area, until the itching stops and the pain is calmed. Then let the limb rest for an hour, then put dry wool on it, moistened with water or rose oil, and bind it to a cushion until you are sure that the abscess is hot.
and let the inflammation of the limb rest, and remove the pain, then gently restart the dressing, and a little poultice, and do not constrict it as before; and gently until it is healed.
And if you see that an abscess is red, swollen, painful and has drained completely, and you need a poultice and bandage, then reapply it as you did the first time.
And if there is no improvement in the limb after what we have said, do not loosen it for three or four or five or seven days; and sometimes leave it for twenty days, depending on what one sees, until the break heals, and bring the joining closer to the flesh.
then bind it more tightly than before and fatten the flesh as I said earlier; and if you see that the area dries out more than necessary, know that there will be no healing. boil the joint in hot water each time you release it, every third day, and loosen the ligament a little;
therefore cutting off the blood supply to the limb through this procedure will quickly correct the harm caused by foolish surgeons who incorrectly reset the limb; this is dangerous, and I see no other option but to stop and work correctly.
on various types of fractures. There are many types of fractures, with different shapes and causes;
For there are fractures caused by sword blows that cut the bone all the way down to the shaft below it, similar to what a hatchet or stick does, and this type of fracture is called "haichure".[ITA]
Where the sword cuts the bone without piercing it, and this type of fracture is called "absolute"; and the wound of these two fractures is large or small.
And if there is a hidden impact, or a crack from a stone, or from falling on a stone, or from similar causes.
And if there is a penetrating fracture that approaches the membrane beneath the bone or is on top of it, and this wound is either large or small.[Note: "toile" in Old French can mean "membrane", "fabric", or "canopy". In this context, it likely refers to the membrane (periosteum) that covers the surface of bones. The translator had to make a judgement call on this one.]
And if there is a wound lodged in the bone as fine as a hair, and the crack is small, and for this reason it is called this type of fracture "hairline".[Note: The Old French word "chevous" means "hairs", but can also refer to any thin or fine object. Here, it likely refers to hairs, hence the translation.]
And if the wound is made by striking with a stone, or by falling, or by similar things, and it drives the piece of bone inward, and the place is sunken in like blacksmiths do when they strike anvils; then stones enter inside.  [Note: The Old French word "chaudelier" can refer to various types of craftsmen who work with heated metal, but here it likely refers specifically to blacksmiths.][Note 2: I am not sure if my translation for "li leus chevez" is accurate; the phrase could also mean "the place is hairy", which doesn't make sense in this context. If anyone has a better suggestion, please let me know.]
And this happens more to those who have moist bones in their heads, such as the bones of children;
And this occurs in all kinds of fractures where small pieces are separated, like so; and I will speak of it in its place.
And we recognize all kinds of fractures by the swelling on them, and through inquiry by touch, and by the corrupt flesh that is on top.[NOTE: I translated "char" as flesh since it can refer to any tissue in medical texts from this time period.]
The appearance of the fracture is recognized by this: when one has uncovered the bone and rubbed over it, the fracture appears black.[NOTES: I translated "li brisure" as "the fracture," assuming that "brisure" is being used as a noun here. Also, I translated "capillaire" as "appearance" since this word can mean several things including hair-like or relating to the head.]
In the treatment of a fracture, beware of any adverse symptoms in the patient, such as vomiting bile, loss of consciousness, convulsions, pallor, fever, and redness and protrusion of the eyes, among other things in various conditions; for without doubt, it cannot heal if these are present.
And if you do not see a frightening accident, and you hope for salvation, then begin the cure.
And when the wounded person comes to you first, and it is winter, you should remove the bone before the fourteenth day at the latest that you can.
And if it is in the summer, you should quickly remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the cloth underneath the bone does not become rotten, and the accidents that we have mentioned come.
And if the break of the bone reaches to the cloth that covers the brain, then you must cut open the split part in this way: by taking the patient's head and uncovering the bone as much as you can, and on the surface of the wound as gently as you can,
And if the flow of blood comes when you uncover the bone, or there is an abscess coming, then you should help with what is necessary and that is to fill the opening with cloths soaked in rose oil.[Reformatted for readability] and let the wound rest until the abscess has calmed down, and you are assured of proper blood flow; then begin along the bone to remove, and this is done in two ways: one way is to make a narrow incision in front, and this is the method:
And then make another incision, larger than the first.
And the second way is to have several different cuts, some narrow and others wide, and they should be pointed and made of iron; and work lightly, so as not to wound the flesh.
And if the bone is hard and tough, then you must drill around it so that you provide cuts with terraces (ledges), not going through the bone but stopping at the outer layer of the bone, leaving a margin or circle on the tip that does not allow the tip to go beyond the bone; and you will need several of these, so that each one comes into place according to the thickness of the bone, so that you have terraces for all parts of the bone; and this is the method of the three types of terracing:
The qualities for drilling around the broken bone are: place a awl on the bone, and turn to your hands until you know that the bone is pierced; then move the awl a little further, and do so all around, then cut the space of the bone that is between the holes, and do this as delicately as you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you draw the bone to your hand, or to any of the tools that you have such as tongs, pliers; and make sure that you do not touch the brain or the sutures.
And when you have pierced and pulled out the bone, it is necessary to insert an instrument that resembles a knife but must be more slender and finer than the other knives;
And if there remains any small bones or shards, gently remove them with an instrument; then clean the wound of pus and ointments as we have said.
And the other method of work is as described by Galen, which is safer, and he highly recommends it; here is what he says: It is necessary, firstly, that you uncover a part of the bone, where the break is clearly visible. Once you have uncovered this area, place beneath the tip of this lunate knife, of which the shape is as follows:
And do not saw in one direction, but rather make the cut on two sides, so that the knife faces the bone. Then strike it lightly with a small mallet, cutting through the bone all the way around, taking great care not to damage the tissue beneath.
If it is adhered to the bone, carefully detach it, for it can be removed without causing harm or fear.
And if the break in the bone does not penetrate through to the periosteum (the membrane covering the bone), but rather is only cut from above with fragments remaining, then you must smooth over this roughness and remove the small flakes using a sharp razor, which you should have in various sizes, so that you can choose the most suitable one for each situation depending on the work and shape of the break.
If the king before large razors, and afterward with more fine ones, and do not stop until it is fully done.
In each other case of hair trimming and fine bone breaking, it is necessary to arrange the direction accordingly; and this is not an easy task even for those who have devoted their studies to this art.
And if the abscess is exposed, then you must take a linen cloth of appropriate size for the wound, soak it in rose oil and place it on the wound. Then take another double-layered cloth and soak it in wine and rose oil and place it on top of the first cloth. Do this as gently as possible to avoid causing further harm, then place a bandage over it without tightening it too much, just enough to cover the wound.
and leave it like that for one or two days, until the abscess has subsided, then loosen it and apply medicine, such as lily roots, vetch flour, incense powder, aristolochia, and similar things; and make a powder from these things and put it on the wound, and continue to administer painless medicine.
and make sure that the wound stays clean, not allowing any residue to remain, nor letting pus gather, because when pus forms on the covering of the brain, it will eat away at it and cause great harm to the patient; for when something biting is placed on top of the siphac (a medical term used in this text), it causes necrosis.
Take heed then, if any adverse event befalls the patient, as we have said, there is reason for doubt and fear.
And if no other cause of blackening is present but from the medicine that has been applied, which may have such a power, then take a part of honey and three parts of rose oil, mix it with one cloth, and place it on the siphac (a medical term used in this text).[ST1] then treat it with various treatments until it is healed.
Know that sometimes the two parts of the nose above are broken, or one of them, because there are two bones; and the one below is cartilaginous, and does not break but only becomes swollen or twisted, and then heals.
And if one of the two parts is broken, you should insert your little finger or the nostril's opening into the break, and push it back into place with your index finger, until the nose regains its natural shape.[*] and do this gently, taking care that the patient does not feel pain from your actions.
And if the break is in the upper part of the nose, and your finger cannot reach it, you should use a small piece of wood to push it back into place.[*]
And if the fracture is in two parts, make it like new again, and hasten to restore it on the first day, if you are able;
If not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the abscess has subsided, then apply a bandage of linen cloth to the swelling if the fracture is in one part.
Or place one [bandage] on the other side if the fracture is there; and let the bandages be thick enough to fill the openings of the nose.[source_author](Guido of Arezzo)
And some restorers say that one should moisten the bandages with butter and change them every day. This does not seem right to me, but it is necessary that they are moistened in the preparation of egg white and powdered mold; then leave the bandage until the bone is healed and the cartilage hardened.
And sometimes goose feathers are placed in the nose instead of bandages, with a soft cloth around it, and this holds the fracture together, and the patient blows through it; do what you will.[source\_author](Guido of Arezzo)
And if pustulent abscesses come to the nose while you are working, put either cerote or cotton soaked in rose oil, or in a piece of lily root.
And if no abscess comes, put an emplaster on the outside, made of chamomile flour and powdered incense, congealed with egg white, then place light wicks on top, but do not bind the nose.
And if the break of the nose is small and it is broken into small pieces, extract it with appropriate instruments, then stitch the wound and cure it of foreign matter and dead flesh, and suture it, using appropriate plasters and ointments.
And if there is no wound inside the nose, then cure it with bandages and put in splints of wood until it is healed.
about the fracture of the jaw
When the lower jaw is dislocated, and there is no wound above it, and the fracture is not present but only a protrusion inside, it can be easily recognized.
If the fracture is on the right side, you should put your index finger in the patient's mouth; and if the fracture is on the left side of the jaw, insert your index finger of the right hand, and gently push the fracture back into place, and align it with the other hand from the outside.
And if the jaw fracture is separated into two parts, you must apply extension to both parts until they are aligned.[df-note] Note: I translated "desevree" as "separated" and "extension" as "applied force to stretch or extend a part of the body."
And if there is movement of the teeth or a fracture, then bind them with a golden or silver or silk thread, and apply a cerate on the broken jaw, and place a double bandage over it. Place a large well-made star-shaped object or a piece of leather of equal size, long and wide according to the jaw, and tie it up high on the head as tightly as possible, and instruct the patient to rest and eat light foods.
And if you see the figure changing, unbind it on the third day, and then realign what has become misaligned; and apply a plaster on top, with powder from the mill and plenty of egg or chickpea flour, after removing the wax; and place light linen on top of the plaster, and if the plasters dry out, and the patient's condition does not change, leave it on until it is healed; it is often healed in three weeks.
And if abscesses come, treat them as we have said many times.
And if there is a fracture and wound at the same time, see if any piece of bone has been removed from it; then carefully remove it with suitable instruments.[Read More](https://raghavkansha.github.io/)
And if the wound is narrow, widen it with fire as necessary.[Read More](https://raghavkansha.github.io/)[ ](https://raghavkansha.github.io/)
And when you have removed all these pieces, and none remain, then stitch the wound, if it is large, and apply one of appropriate plasters to it, to help heal the flesh, until it has healed.
