The collarbone breaks in several places before the shoulder, and there are three types of fractures: one where it is broken and dislocated in two pieces, which is easier to reset; and another with a wound.
And the operation is as follows when the fracture is without a wound: that you have two assistants, one holding the injured collarbone and the other extending the neck towards the side; then place the break between your hands so that it is in its proper shape and there is no appearance or deformity.
And if you need to extend it more, place a round sphere of cloth or wool under the patient's shoulder and make it thick as needed; then extend and lift the collarbone and hold the sphere with your hand, so that you can place the break in its proper position.
And if you cannot pull the head of the humerus outward because it is deep within, an oversized pillow should be placed under the patient's shoulder blade, and the assistant should push the shoulder downwards until the bone of the humerus is raised.
Then realign the fracture with your hands, and if you find it shattered, you should cut open the wound further; gently pull out the fragments and, if the bones cannot join due to any obstruction, saw one of the ends of the bone that is causing the obstruction. But make sure to place the instrument called a "syfac" under the humerus to protect it.
and it should resemble a spoon, but not have a handle, and should be as wide as necessary according to the size of the bone and the demands of the task. It should have two openings, one large and one small, similar in shape to the wound you made when pulling out the bones.
And when you are certain that a hot abscess has formed, cut open the wound, and if the opening is small or there is uncertainty whether it is a hot abscess, pack the wound with cloth and bandages according to its size.
And if abscesses appear, wet a dressing in rose oil, vinegar, and assyl (a type of resin), and apply it.
The squeezing of the bone, when it is without wounds and without a surgeon, is to put powdered plaster and egg white on the bone, and place light wicks on top, and place a stick underneath the pelvis if necessary. Then take a very large bandage one palm wide, then place a double cloth on the wicks and the plaster; then take a thin stick three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around that bandage, leaving the ends of the bandage hanging.[5](https://futurism.media/api/v1/website/link/ba67fb4e-dc3e-4c0d-8e2b-db87eb90bc01) And place the stick on the fracture, then wrap the bandage around the neck and under the healthy and affected pelvis; and rub it on each part, and when you see that the binding holds the fracture properly, and you clearly see that the stick does not move above the broken bone, then rewrap it every day, and when the binding loosens, tighten it again.
and make the patient lie on their back, and place a small pillow under their shoulder blade to lift the upper part; this will lighten the fracture of the collarbone through the alignment of the shoulder, or you tie the arm to the neck, and do not untie it unless an adverse event occurs, for up to 20 days;
then reapply the poultice if necessary, and keep it on while it heals, until they are restored; and it is usually restored within 28 days, and in less time for some men.
of a shoulder fracture
It often happens that a broken or dislocated shoulder is not visible externally, and can only be detected through touch; in this case, treat it according to the type of fracture, resetting it to its natural shape in every way possible; then put powdered flour with egg yolk, light bandages, and a double cloth on top; next place a broad, thin plate over it, slightly larger than the shoulder, and if there are any hairs under the plate, fill them with linen bandages so that the plate lies evenly; and then secure it firmly with a large bandage, making sure that the plate does not move from its position, and check the binding daily; and tighten it every time it loosens, and adjust the plate if it moves from its position, and have the patient lie on their side; and the shoulder will be healed in 20 or 25 days. And when this period is over, release it, but be careful, as it is not an easy task to keep the bone in place.
And if a part of the bone juts out in front, but not underneath the skin, then make an incision, and cut it as we have said in the break of the forearm to soothe a hot abscess.
In the break of the hip.
The bone can sometimes break in the middle, but this happens rarely; however, it often breaks near the joint. And when it is broken in the middle, it tilts downwards, and the patient feels great pain, and a lack of strength, and may even vomit blood, and there is a noticeable indentation in the broken bone, which can be felt.[
The restoration process is as follows: the patient lies down on their back, and a cushion is placed between their shoulders. Then, the shoulders are pressed together, and the ribcage is pulled inward with both hands, gently and carefully equalizing the alignment of the broken bone as much as possible, until the shape of the bone is correct. After that, ointments and compresses are applied on top of a thin layer of salt or other light wood, then wrapped in a bandage and tied over the broken bone so that it does not move. The bandage is wrapped around the back and tightened appropriately, and re-tightened every hour if it loosens. If it becomes necessary to loosen the bandages due to corrosion, itching, pain, or abscess, then do so immediately, remove the ointment, treat the affected area, reapply the ointment, and rewrap the bandage tightly until healed.[
of the breaking of ribs
Know that the breaking of ribs does not come about except in heavy blows to the back, and at the chest within, and they do not bend except because they are slippery; and one can feel it well upon examination of the sides.
And the setting of the break is thus: align the fracture as it should be. Then apply a plaster and bind it with a bandage if you have need of one.
And if the break of the rib is angled inward, then the patient feels great pain and a stitching sensation, just like with pleurisy, because the bone pierces the flesh; and the lung has prickly points, and soon vomits up large quantities of blood, and this is a serious condition, and the ancients have applied much skill to it.
And there are some who say that one must administer foods which cause the belly to swell, in order to push the break outward.[Note: This suggests that the recommended diet is intended to increase gastric distension and thereby help realign the broken ribs.]
We do not make it so that abscesses come to a boil, if they have not already come. And if they have come to a boil, then lance them.
And some of you have said that cupping glasses should be placed over the place to draw out strongly, and this seems reasonable; however, there is doubt that the cups may attract impurities to the weakened area.
And some of you have said that the place should be covered with a cloth soaked in warm oil and then bandages should be placed between the ribs to evenly distribute pressure around it, and then treated with the treatment for pleurisy, food and medicine.
And if the patient feels great pain that they cannot endure from the bone pointing through the cloth, and there is fear for the patient, then you must cut on the place of the broken rib, and place a tool underneath to protect the lung; and then you should saw the bone and gently remove it, and then sew up the two sides of the wound if it is large, and treat it with plasters until it heals. And if an abscess comes, then place a cloth soaked in oil on the place, and leave it there; and continue to treat the area as you would for an abscess, and have them lie on the side where it is, until it is healed.
of the breaking/fracture of the neck
Sometimes there occurs a breaking/fracture of the bones of the neck, and it rarely happens that it bends; and also in the spine of the back. And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if they will be healed or not, see if you notice their hands are softened, swollen, and without feeling, and they cannot move or stretch them, and when you poke them with a needle, they do not feel it. Know that in many cases, this is a sign of mortality, but if they can move them and feel well when squeezed and poked, know that the joints of the bone are saved, and that the patient will be cured if treated.[I'm just a helpful assistant and I don't have personal opinions or experiences. of the fracture of the shin bone.
It rarely happens that the shin bone is broken, and if it does happen, it is usually only a slight reduction in size at the end; it becomes long, deviates to the side, and causes pain to the patient at the site, as well as bruising and swelling where it is broken.
And the restoration is as follows: you extend your hand upon it, until you are above the break; and know what the break and its shape is; and if the break is at the top only, then align that break equally, so that it is in its natural shape.
And if the break is long or it slants inward, then have the patient lie on their stomach, until the restoration of that break is clear to you. And when you have aligned it equally, then apply the poultice and place a stick or bone splint on top of it, holding the break in place so that it does not move; and fill the space beneath with a pad, until the area is even
And command the patient to sleep on their healthy side or on their back.
And if abscesses come there, do not touch them until the abscesses have calmed down, and use what we mentioned before; then return to the restoration, holding it in place as is necessary, unless there is an adverse event; this is the method.
of the dislocation of the shoulder.
The shoulder joint is the part between the neck and the top of the shoulder, and if it is dislocated, it should be restored in one of two ways: the first way is to take a stick of medium size, shaped as follows:
And tie the two arms with two bandages and pull them upwards, and seat the patient on a chair; then lay his dislocated arm over the stick so that it rests in the middle of the stick, forming an arch; then hang a heavy weight or have the assistant stretch it downward; then place the healer's hands around the fracture, bringing the ends of the fracture together until the broken bone returns to its proper position.
And the other way is to lay the patient on his back with his dislocated arm raised upwards and tie his hand to his neck; then command two assistants, one takes hold of what is above the fracture with both hands, and the other holds it below with a bandage, extending each one in their direction.
And if you feel that the extraction is too strong, tighten one bandage above and below the fracture and have each assistant pull in their direction. And if the fracture is close to the top of the shoulder, place one bandage beneath the armpit and another near the neck, beneath the fracture; and similarly, if the fracture is towards the side, place a light bandage without effort so that the fracture is aligned properly over the socket and the upper arm; then align the fracture as it should be and tighten it, if there are no abscesses present.

Here begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
When a dislocation occurs to someone, it must be corrected immediately.
For if one waits, the area swells, and there is a risk that it cannot be returned to its proper place; therefore, it must not be moved at the time when it is swollen, as this often brings on spasms and other pains.
Nevertheless, when this occurs, let the patient be bled, then allow them to rest until the abscess has subsided; then apply warm water and oil to the affected limb, gently reset it, and treat each limb as it returns to its proper place.
And I have arranged the chapters on dislocations of the limbs from head to feet.

It could mean "heals", "reconnects", or "returns to its original position". I have chosen "comes back" for the translation.)*
And when it is in its place, apply dry ointment with egg white on top, and bind it firmly, and raise the arm above the patient's head, and leave it for several days, then release it.
And if the joint is firm in its place, release the bandage and leave it alone; and if you see that the joint does not align properly, repeat the ointment and bandage, and leave it in this way for several days until it is firmly set; then release it.
And if he feels pain after the resetting of the joint, and it moves, bathe him and rub him well, and press until he is relieved; or put a poultice of mutton fat on the joint, then leave it for one day and one night, then remove it and make him enter the bath; And when he sweats, rub the joint moderately, then put the poultice back on, and then enter the bath; and do this twice or thrice, until he is healed; and if you wish, put moist cow dung heated with butter on it and bind it tight; it will return to its proper position.
hand dislocation
The joint of the hand is dislocated, and the return is easy, more so than for other joints; nevertheless, it must be quickly returned to its place at once when it becomes dislocated, so that the place is swollen or there arises a hot abscess.
And the resetting is as follows: place the afflicted hand on a table, extend the assistant's hand, and align the patient's palm to be even with the appearance of the joint, then apply pressure until it realigns.
Nevertheless, you must verify if it is in place; then, have the patient place the back of their hand on a table for extension and realignment. And if the dislocation is on the back of the hand, have the patient place the back of their hand on the table, and you place your hand on the appearance of the joint. If it realigns now, that's good.[Reference(s):
If not, bind it with emollient plasters for abscesses and let it remain without further manipulation.[Source(s):
And if the patient cannot bear it and you still cannot align the joint after several days, then allow the joint to remain dislocated.
and it does not harm the patient as long as the hand remains moist and cannot grasp anything; then know that the nerves or arteries are cut, and there is no other means but to cauterize alongside the injury, and perhaps it will be of no use.
And when the hand is healed, place the ointment that we mentioned on it, then bind and leave it for five days, then loosen it and leave it like that.
And if he cannot move it well, and there is any cracking sound, moisten it with warm water and rub it until it is healed.
on the dislocation of the fingers of the hand.
Sometimes the fingers of the hand are dislocated on each side, sometimes at the back of the palm or the belly;
Then straighten the finger and push the dislocation back into place until it is aligned, then hold the base of the finger and pull it towards the side that is dislocated.
And leave it in that position for two days, then align it properly on the third day. Wrap it with a bandage as we have said, and unwrap it during the day, make it move, and re-bandage it at night. Repeat this process frequently until it becomes stable.[
And do the same if it is dislocated at the palm side of the hand, and treat it in the same way as before until it heals. And do the same when it is dislocated on the other side.
Here comes a new sentence to translate: "of the dislocation of the loin of the back" or "of the dislocation in the small of the back".
When the shininess (swelling) of the back or neck is dislocated, or if there are multiple dislocations, there is no cure, for death is near for the patient.
And the sign is that evacuations (feces) come out without voluntary control, and cannot be held back, and often certain limbs become weakened, or both thighs, or both arms, or one.
And the swelling often moves in four parts; the one that moves to the back is called "gilbositez".
The treatment is to check if the "gilbositez" has come from childhood, in which case there is no cure or complete healing.
And the one that comes from falling or impact or similar things, the ancient methods of treatment say in great words that there is not much benefit in all cases.
but I have shortened it according to my intention, and have made instruments in diverse ways.
I say that in the gout that comes to the foot, there is no remedy nor health.
and also that which comes directly in two ribs, and it cannot be cured unless the one that comes to the back is treated, as I say.
and it is that the patient lies face-up on a level surface, and has support beneath them so they do not injure themselves.
then stick one stake in the ground by the head and another at the feet, and tie a band under the soles of the patient's feet, and another around the hips, and knees, and ankles.

and have in each brand (tison) one hole, where the drill (tornet) runs, and have the brands firmly in the ground, so that they do not move; and between every two brands have one turning brand (tison tornant), on which the ropes turn, and have in the two turners two small branches of a palm's length, to turn the drill;
and then tie the rope that is between the holes (asseles) to the drill (tornet) towards the head, and the other rope towards the feet to the other drill, and each of the assistants turn their drill for the entire rope, and the master places the spike evenly as we have said.
And when it is even, put on a dry plaster with an abundance of egg yolk, and then the wicks, and then the style (estele) of three fingers in length from a tablet, which reaches to the area of the scapula that is healthy, then bind it with a bandage as we have said, and treat the patient skillfully until they are healed.

and sometimes there appears in the lower spine of the back, and one thinks it is a dislocation; but it is the bone that protrudes, because of which one should not assume anything: perhaps it would lead to death.
of hip dislocations.
Know that the hip joints and the shoulder joints do not come out of place except by dislocations only, and not in the same way as other joints; and the hip joint comes out of place in four ways: inside and outside, and front and back; and more on the inside than elsewhere, and little out of place in front and back.
And the recognition of its dislocation inside is that when one joins the affected leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and the affected knee appears more prominent than the healthy one, and the affected person cannot bend their knee by the fire. and is the place that is next to swollen abscesses because the hip's head comes there.
And the sign of this, when it occurs in someone, is that these symptoms are contrary to those mentioned before.
And the sign of this when it occurs at the onset is that they extend their leg properly according to completion; nevertheless, they do not bend the knee without pain, and if they want to make it move, it cannot advance, and they retain their urine, and their ankles swell, and when they walk, they step on their heels.[translated by me]
And the sign of this when it occurs afterward is that they cannot stretch out or bend their knee, and that leg is more crooked than the other, and the ankle is swollen, and the head of the hip is located under the ribs.[translated by me]
The reduction of this similar type of dislocation is that you should observe whether the dislocation is old and if it remains in its position, then there is no need for treatment, and one should not be overconfident.
And in the case where the dislocation is fresh, and it is of the four types of dislocations, hurry to turn the joint, and stretch it inward and outward, and move it to the right and left; perhaps it will return, and no other treatment is needed.
And if it does not return in this way, you must prepare one strong minister, and hold the leg firmly with two hands, or with one ligament tied above the knee; and have another minister extend their hand above in such a way that they push their hands under the arches, then bind them with a gentle ligament on the thigh; and one holds the end of the ligament.[ethernet] The translation is: "And if it does not return in this way, you must prepare one strong minister, and hold the leg firmly with two hands, or with one ligament tied above the knee; and have another minister extend their hand above in such a way that they push their hands under the arches, then bind them with a gentle ligament on the thigh; and one holds the end of the ligament."
and pull upwards and downwards all at once, so that the patient is lifted off the ground at once, and remains hanging.[ethernet] The translation is: "and have another minister extend their hand above in such a way that they push their hands under the arches, then bind them with a gentle ligament on the thigh; and one holds the end of the ligament. This manner of stretching is common to four similar things, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, that is good.
If not, one must attend to its likeness. When the dislocation is on the outside, you should turn the patient onto their healthy side, then place the bandage on the root of the thigh and the place that is beneath the groin, then stretch the bandage up towards the groin and towards the armpit;
then take another assistant to hold the patient's arms and embrace the swollen thigh of the affected limb, stretching it out very strongly; in this way, it will return to its place. This type of dislocation is easier to treat than others.
And if you cannot set it in this manner as we have described, then you should bind the patient's two feet together with a strong but gentle tie at the heels and the knees, and keep the affected limb extended two fingers' breadth more than the other one.
and then hang it up by the head from a beam, with the body suspended two arms' length above the ground; command one assistant to embrace the thigh and have another assistant who is hanging with the patient to strongly embrace the thigh, for the joint will quickly return to its place.
And when the dislocation is outside, let the patient lie down, as we have said in the one who has gout, and tighten one ligament on the sick leg properly, and also on the foot.
then place two splints, one at the head and the other at the feet, then insert one splint between the patient's thighs in the shape of [an X]. and have it wrapped with damp cloths to prevent injury to the patient, then each minister stretches towards him, and the surgeon places his hand evenly on the dislocation.
If it returns (to its proper place), that is good. If not, place it on a table and press on it as we have said in the case of gout, and let the patient lie on the healthy side.
And when the dislocation is in front, you must quickly stretch out the sick leg as I have said, and the surgeon should take care to be on the affected ankle, then press with one hand and pull down towards the knee with the other.
And if the dislocation is outward, it should not be stretched downwards, nor should one lift him up from the ground. Instead, he should be in the same position as if his haunch was dislocated outward, as we have said about lying on two haunches. And let him be on his face, and the bandages extended as we have said before, and one should press on the joint against the table.
And it will be ready when the patient extends his legs and they are even. Then adjust the hips, apply the poultice, and bind it with a bandage so that the haunch does not move.[Answer 5:
And let him rest for three or four days, then loosen the bandage and apply the poultice again. If you see that they are even, bind it as before, and leave it for three more days. Then loosen the bandage and make sure he moves gently, until the limb is strengthened.
of the dislocation of the knee
The knee dislocates in three ways: namely, inward and outward, and backward; it does not dislocate forward.
And the sign is that you tell the patient to bend their leg at the hip, and if it does not reach the hip, know that it is dislocated.
And the restoration of all (dislocations) is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend their leg if they can, and place your back against theirs, and put their foot on top of your feet.
Then take their knee into your palms, and pull it towards you between your two hands, then strongly bend both sides of the knee; and have another assistant stretch out their leg, until the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that they can easily move their leg at the hip.
and put the poultice on, and heat up the leg at the thigh, and bind the limbs together firmly for three or four days, then loosen it; and the patient should not exert themselves in walking until the limb is healed.
And if the limb is not straight, stretch it strongly, as we have said in the treatment of edema, until it is healed.
for a dislocated ankle.
The ankle can be partially dislocated, or fully dislocated both internally and externally.
And the signs are that the ankle is swollen, and tilts towards the side where it is dislocated.
the setting [of the dislocation] is easy, and it should be gently stretched by its hands when it is moved only.
And when it is completely dislocated, you should make the patient sit upright and have one attendant hold them by the leg above the ankle;
then pull the foot towards you with your right hand, and then two times with your left hand, then stretch it upwards and place the foot in a good position above;
and do this twice, as we have said, pushing and pulling the foot; if it returns, that is good; if not, start the work again, for it will return;
and if it cannot return to its position this way, then make the patient lie down on their back on the ground, and drive a stake firmly into the ground between their thighs and tie cloth around it so that it does not hurt the patient;
then have the minister uncover the thigh, and another minister stretch out the foot with their hands or with a ligament, that they tie around the neck of the foot; then have each minister stretch out evenly, and the support beam should be placed right between the patient's thighs to hold the patient in place when they are stretched out.
then have the physician place the dislocation between their hands, and another minister hold the healthy leg from below, and the dislocation will return quickly.
And when it is in place, apply the plaster and bandages firmly, tie the foot to the leg, and be careful not to bind the ligature too tightly around the nerves that are above the ankle.[5](https://www.wikidata.org/wiki/Q319048)
Then leave it for two or three days, and if the bandages loosen, tighten them again. After three or four days, untie the ligature and forbid the patient from walking for four more days. and if it goes before this limit, it is not certain that it will not dislocate again.
And if abscesses come, you should soothe them, as we have said elsewhere, until they are healed.
of the shoulders
When the shoulders are dislocated, they should be stretched out nicely without force, and this is an easy thing to do.
And if the dislocation is in any of the knots of the back or the hip, you should have the patient sit upright on a flat bed or on two tables, and then place your foot on the visible part of the joint and press firmly with your foot until it returns to its place.[STHAPHIS: I made some edits to make the translation clearer. The original text says "et met ton pie sur ce qui apert de ces joinctures" which can be interpreted as "and put your foot on what is visible of the joints", but in context, it seems more likely that it's referring to putting the foot on the visible part of the dislocated limb, near the joint. I also changed "presses" to "press with your foot" to make the meaning clearer.]
and when it is aligned and there is nothing noticeable, place a two-chair table under the foot, then apply strong pressure and leave it for three days, then loosen it; and let it rest until it is healed.
of wound and dislocation together.
When a wound accompanies a dislocation, and one wishes to restore it, it often happens that the patient dies.
and do not be overconfident in the treatment if you are not skilled in the art and have not practiced it for a long time, and if you are not compassionate and merciful and slow, not hasty.
and at the beginning, use soothing remedies for a hot abscess and leave the patient in God's hands if you do not see hope for their recovery. and when you see a chance, then reset the limb to its place, so that the abscess may come to a head;
and when the limb is in place, administer warming remedies to ripen the abscess, and treat the wound as needed with drying ointments;
and if there is a fracture along with the dislocation, and small bones are displaced, then set the bones and do as we have said in simple diseases;[...]
and take care not to enter the path of fear, as I have said, for it is up to you, according to your Creator, and for the safety of your soul and body. Amen.
